(c)	It shall be unlawful for any person to drink or have in his possession an open container of any alcoholic beverage: 
(1)	On any public street, sidewalk, park or other public place within the county, or upon or within any motor vehicle on the streets, sidewalks, parks and public places of the county; or 
(2)	While on private property, open to public view, without the express permission of the owner, agent or person in lawful possession thereof. 
( Ord. No. 244 , § 46, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-77. - Prohibited practices. 
(a)	No consumption on the premises licensee shall engage in any of the following practices: 
(1)	The giving away of any alcoholic beverages in conjunction with the sale of any other alcoholic beverages; 
(2)	The sale of two or more alcoholic beverages for a single price or the sale of all the alcoholic beverages a customer can or desire to drink. 
( Ord. No. 244 , § 47, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-78. - Brown bag establishments prohibited. 
Brown bag establishments as defined in this chapter shall be prohibited within the county. 
( Ord. No. 244 , § 48, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-79. - Excise taxes. 
(a)	There is imposed by the county an excise tax on the first sale or use of malt beverages in the county, as follows: 
(1)	Where malt beverages, commonly known as tap or draft beer, are sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, a tax of $6.00 on each container containing not more than 15½ gallons. 
(2)	Where malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans or other containers, except barrel or bulk containers, a tax of $0.05 per 12 ounces and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 12 ounces. 
(b)	There is imposed by the county an excise tax on the first sale or use of wine in the county at a rate of $0.22 per liter and proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(c)	Reserved. 
(d)	The excise taxes provide for in this section shall be imposed upon and paid by the licensed wholesale dealer. Such taxes shall be paid on or before the 20th day of the month following the month in which the alcoholic beverages are sold or disposed of by the wholesaler within the county. 
( Ord. No. 244 , § 49, 2-23-2016) 
Secs. 6-80—6-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DISTILLED SPIRITS 

Sec. 6-101. - Short title. 
This article shall be known and may be cited as "Upson County Distilled Spirits." 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 1, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-102. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Alcoholic beverage means and includes all distilled spirits defined in this section. 
Alcohol beverage caterer means a license holder issued an alcohol beverage caterer's license by the county under the authority of O.C.G.A. tit. 3, ch. 11. 
Board of commissioners means the county commissioners of the county. 
Brown bag establishment means any restaurant, or other establishment providing food or entertainment in the normal course of business, or premises licensed hereunder, and in which the owners or their agents knowingly allow patrons to bring in and consume the patrons' alcoholic beverages. 
Calendar year means the period of time from the date of issuance of a license on or after each January 1st to the date of December 31st of the year of issuance of said license. 
Church means any permanent place of public religious worship. 
County means the County of Upson, and when used in a geographical sense means the territorial limits of the unincorporated county. 
County manager means the county manager of the board of commissioners of Upson County, Georgia. 
Deliver means to give, surrender, to carry and hand over. 
Distilled spirits means any alcoholic beverage obtained by distillation or containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume including, but not limited to, all fortified wines. 
Election day means any general election, primary election, run-off election, special election, or referendum within the unincorporated areas of the county. 
Interest includes any pecuniary interest and any ownership interest, whether present or future, whole or partial, legal or beneficial, contingent or vested, direct or indirect, and any right, power, or authority of control. 
Licensed premises means and includes not only the room wherein alcoholic beverages are sold or served but also the outdoor area within the property lines as approved by the board of commissioners for sales and consumption of alcoholic beverages. 
Licensee means and includes an individual licensee and in the case of a partnership, limited liability company, or corporation includes both the partnership, limited liability company and corporation and the named licensee. 
Majority stockholder means the person, if any, who owns more than 50 percent of the voting stock of a corporation; if no person owns more than 50 percent of the voting stock of a corporation, the majority stockholder is the person owning more of the voting stock than any other person; and if two or more persons each own the same amount of the voting stock of a corporation and each own more of the voting stock than any other person, then any one of such persons may act as the majority stockholder. 
Moral turpitude means conduct contrary to justice, honesty, modesty, or good morals. 
Named licensee means the person acting as such for a partnership, limited liability, or corporation pursuant to section 6-105, procedure for issuance. 
Package means a bottle, can, keg, barrel, or other original consumer container. 
Restaurant means any establishment which is licensed to sell alcoholic beverages and which derives at least 50 percent of its total annual gross income from the sale of on-site prepared meals or food and which has a seating capacity of not less than 25 persons. 
School means state or county school or such other schools (public or private) as teach subjects commonly taught in common schools and colleges of this state, and inclusive of daycare centers that may supervise five or more children at one time. 
Sheriff means the sheriff of the county. 
Special event permit means a special event permit applied for and issued in accordance with the requirements of O.C.G.A. tit. 3, ch. 11 to a licensed alcoholic beverage caterer. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 2, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-103. - Penalty. 
Any person who violates any provision of this article shall upon conviction be punished as provided in the Upson County Code. Any such punishment, if imposed, shall be in addition to and not in lieu of any license suspension or revocation under this chapter. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 3, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-104. - Licensing. 
(a)	Required, classifications, fee, duration. 
(1)	Required. It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer for sale any distilled spirit by the drink for consumption on the premises within the county except under a valid license issued under this section and in compliance with the provisions set forth below. 
(2)	Classification, fee. Classes of licenses issued under this chapter, activities permitted and regulated thereunder, and the annual license fees, shall be as follows: 
a.	Distilled spirits (sale by the drink for consumption on the premises only: 
Annual license fee ..... $1,000.00 
Renewal fee ..... 1,000.00 
b.	Alcohol beverage caterer's license ..... 1,000.00 
Renewal fee ..... 1,000.00 
c.	Special event permit ..... 100.00 
Duration, proration. All licenses issued under this chapter shall be issued on a calendar-year basis; and all licenses shall expire at 12:00 midnight on December 31 of the year in which they are issued. For all licenses issued from January 1st and June 30th, the full annual license fee shall be due and payable. For all licenses issued between July 1st and December 31st, the annual license. 
(3)	Fees shall be one-half of the stated annual fees. Notwithstanding the month in which a license is issued, the license shall still expire at the time and date set forth above. Each special event permit shall be valid for a 24-hour period. 
(4)	Application fees. Each application for a license under this section, except in the case of a special event, shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable application fee in the amount of $100.00. 
(5)	Payment of fee. The application fee shall be paid at the time the application is filed and shall not be refunded under any circumstances. An applicant may pay the annual license fee at the time that the application is filed; and in such event the annual license fee shall be refunded if the license applied for is not issued. If the annual license fee is not paid at the time of application, the annual license fee shall be paid prior to the issuance of the license by the board of commissioners and no later than 14 days after notification of approval of the license by the board of commissioners. 
(6)	Modification of fees . The annual license fee and application fee set out hereinabove may be increased or decreased by resolution of the board of commissioners. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 4, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-105. - Procedure for issuance. 
A license issued to an individual under this article shall be issued in the name of the individual. A license issued to a partnership, limited liability company or corporation of any type shall be issued in the name of the partnership, limited liability company or corporation and in the name of one or more of the partners or majority stockholder who shall be named licensee. Provided however, that all partners, majority stockholders, and each principal officer of a partnership, limited liability company or corporation must meet the qualifications of an individual licensee, as provided in the following section. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 5, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-106. - Qualifications. 
(a)	A licensee must be at least 21 years of age, of good moral character, and a citizen of the United States. 
(b)	A licensee shall not have been convicted within the past ten years of any felony, any misdemeanor involving moral turpitude or criminal offense relating to alcoholic beverages, underage sales, taxes or gambling. A licensee shall not have been convicted within the past four years of any other misdemeanor or violation of a county ordinance. This subsection shall apply with respect to the laws of this state, other states, the United States, and other countries. A plea of nolo contendere or the forfeiture of a bond shall be considered a conviction for purposes of this subsection. The board of commissioners may at its discretion, waive the conviction of a misdemeanor or county ordinance for purposes of this subsection if the board of commissioners determines that the violation does not have a bearing on the applicant's fitness for a license. 
(c)	A licensee or a member of his/her immediate family shall not have been denied or had revoked, within the five years preceding his application, any license to sell alcoholic beverages issued by any governmental entity. 
(d)	A licensee shall be the owner of the premises to be licensed or the holder of a lease thereon for substantially the same period to be covered by the license, and shall possess a current occupation tax certificate for said premises. 
(e)	Any person having two convictions for selling alcoholic beverage to a minor within a three-year period shall not be eligible for a license. 
(f)	If the licensee is a corporation or limited liability company, its officers, any designated agent or manager must meet the qualifications of subsections (a) through (e) hereinabove. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 6, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-107. - Application. 
(a)	Forms, contents. 
(1)	Each applicant shall apply to the county manager for a license by written application. All applications for licenses shall be made upon application forms provided by the board of commissioners. All applications shall contain a full and complete and sworn and notarized statement by each applicant of all material facts relevant to the requirements of this article. In addition, each applicant shall provide a government issued photo I.D. or driver's license which can be photocopied and the copy shall be attached to the application. Each applicant and any corporate officers or shareholders otherwise required to be fingerprinted shall submit themselves to the sheriff's department, where a complete set of fingerprints shall be taken. 
(2)	All applications must be filed at least 30 days prior to the date to be considered by the board. 
(3)	Applications will be considered and licenses granted only at the regular meeting of the board of commissioners, unless otherwise approved by the board. 
(4)	Each application shall include, in addition to all other application fees, cash or money order in the amount charged by the Georgia Bureau of Investigation made payable to the Upson County Sheriff's Office to cover the cost of each fingerprinting analysis and investigation. 
(b)	Each applicant authorizes the county and its agents to secure from any court, law enforcement agency, or other public agency his criminal and civil history and to use such information in determining whether the license applied for shall be issued. Each applicant further authorizes the county and its agents to use such information in any public hearing with respect to the license applied for, either before or after the issuance of the license. Each applicant waives any right which he would otherwise have to preclude the county or its agents from obtaining and using such information; and each applicant further waives any liability of the county or its agents from obtaining and using such information. It shall be the responsibility of each applicant to provide a verifiable criminal history obtained from Georgia Crime Information Center with each application. 
(c)	Each application shall be accompanied by: 
(1)	A copy of the deed to the premises, if owned by the licensee; 
(2)	A copy of the lease agreement covering the premises to be licensed, if leased by the licensee, showing the term of the lease; 
(3)	In the case of a partnership, a copy of the partnership agreement; 
(4)	In the case of a corporation or limited liability corporation, a copy of the articles of incorporation; 
(5)	A copy of the occupation tax application and receipt for all due occupation taxes, fees, penalties and interest for the premises; and 
(6)	For a consumption on the premises license, a statement of the seating capacity or occupancy capacity of the premises where the license will be used. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 7, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-108. - Investigation; hearing. 
(a)	A copy of each application for a license under this article shall be referred within two business days after filing to the sheriff's department. The sheriff's department shall make a thorough investigation concerning any applicants hereunder if individuals, and the officers and the designated agent or manager, if the applicant is a corporation or limited liability company, and shall submit the results of the investigation promptly to the county manager on behalf of the board of commissioners. 
(b)	No application for an original license shall be considered by the county manager until after a public hearing has been held thereon by the board of commissioners, after notice as provided in subsections (c) and (d) of this section. 
(c)	Except in the case of a special event permit for which the board has allowed a waiver, a designated Upson County staff member shall post on the premises to be licensed a notice. The notice shall be posted for at least 15 days prior to the date of the hearing. The notice shall be on a board or metal sign to be furnished by the county having a surface of not less than 12 square feet. The staff member shall ensure that a photograph of the notice is taken and provided to the Upson County clerk. The sign shall include the following: 
(1)	That an application for a license to sell distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises has been filed with the county; 
(2)	The type of license applied for; 
(3)	The time and place of the public hearing to be held on such license application; 
(4)	The name of the proposed licensee; and 
(5)	The name and telephone number of the county staff member where additional information may be obtained. 
Such sign shall be placed at least three feet above the ground and facing the most traveled street. The applicant will deposit $100.00 with the county which will be refunded upon the return of the sign. 
(d)	The county shall, on behalf of an applicant for an original license, publish in the official legal organ of the county at least 15 days prior to the hearing, a notice containing the same information as required in the posted notice under subsection (c) of this section. This notice shall be printed in letters no smaller than ten-point capital and lower case with at least a one-inch, two-column arrangement. The applicant for an original license shall pay to the county the expense of publication at the time the application is made. 
(e)	Prior to the date of the hearing, the applicant shall furnish to the board of commissioners a copy of the advertisement required by subsection (d) of this section and a sworn statement of the size of, location of, and information on the sign required by subsection (c) of this section. 
(f)	The board of commissioners may require additional investigations, reports and information from county departments and other public agencies as may be deemed necessary to evaluate compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(g)	Following the filing of a complete application, the submission of the sheriff department's report and any other reports deemed necessary by the board of commissioners, the notice and advertisement required by subsections (c) and (d), and the public hearing required by subsection (b), the board of commissioners shall act on the application after considering the standards and guidelines set forth in this article. 
(h)	Any applicant aggrieved by the decision of the board of commissioners regarding a license application may request that the board of commissioners reconsider its decision after another hearing in which the applicant shall have the opportunity to present evidence and cross-examine opposing witnesses. Such request for reconsideration must be presented to the county manager in writing and must be made within 30 days of the date of the decision prompting such request. 
(i)	Any person making a false statement in any application for a license, or false statement in connection with renewal thereof, shall be guilty of an offense and punished as provided by state law relating to false swearing; and further, a license if previously granted or renewed, may be revoked for the violation. It shall be an offense for any person to give other than the true and correct legal name of the intended licensee; and a conviction for violation thereof shall be punished as provided for in this chapter. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 8, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-109. - Renewals. 
(a)	Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, applications for renewal of licenses shall be made and considered in the same manner as applications for original licenses. No application fee shall be required for a renewal of license. Renewal applicants will be required to submit a current criminal history report from the Georgia Crime Information Center with all renewal applications. 
(b)	No fingerprints shall be required in the case of an application for renewals. 
(c)	No posting of premises and publication of notice by the applicant shall be required in the case of an application for renewal. 
(d)	An application for renewal may, if such is the case, be in the form of a sworn and notarized statement by the named licensee, on a form provided by the county manager, stating that there have been no changes in any of the information contained in the original application. If there have been any such changes, the application for renewal shall be in the same form as an original application. 
(e)	An application for renewal shall be filed during the month of October. If an existing licensee fails to file for renewal during the month of October, then the licensee shall be required to make application as for an original license. Existing licensees, whose renewal application is filed in October as required in this subsection and approved by the board of commissioners, shall pay the appropriate licensing fee required by this chapter on or before January 1 of the year for which the renewal license has been approved. 
(f)	In making a determination regarding the renewal of a license, the board of commissioners shall consider the standards and guidelines set forth in section 6-115 of this article. 
(g)	At the discretion of the board of commissioners, a public hearing may be required for the renewal of a license if written objections are filed thereto with the county manager at least 15 days before the end of the renewal period. If any such objection is filed, a public hearing shall be held. Prior to such hearing, the county shall publish at public expense a notice in substantially the same form and manner required under subsection (d) of section 6-108. The applicant shall be given written notice of any objection which is filed and such notice shall be served within 48 hours of the filing of the objection by personal service by a deputy sheriff or by registered or certified mail to the named licensee at the licensed premises. In the circumstances referred to in this subsection, the license under which renewal was applied for shall continue to be valid until the board of commissioners acts on the application for renewal if the applicant deposits the amount of the annual license fee for the renewal with the board of commissioners, not later than five days after being notified of the filing of the objection. 
(h)	An applicant for renewal whose application is denied may request reconsideration as provided for in subsection (h) of section 6-108. 
(i)	In addition to the application referred to herein, applicant shall submit a current criminal history report. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 9, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-110. - Transfer. 
(a)	Except as provided in this section, no license issued under this article shall be transferable to any other person or location. 
(b)	If a licensee seeks to move his place of business from the licensee's premises to another place within the county, application shall be made as for an original license. 
(c)	In the case of death of an owner of a license or financial interest therein, such license or interest therein may be transferred to the administrator, executor, or adult heir of the deceased unless the board of commissioners determines that it would otherwise violate this chapter. If the transferee cannot meet all requirements of this chapter, when the time comes to renew the license, it shall not be renewed. 
(d)	Nothing in this section shall prohibit one or more partners in a partnership from retiring therefrom in favor of one or more of the other partners; provided such withdrawal shall not, without application for an issuance of a new license, introduce any new partner or result in any new person acquiring an interest in the licensed business. 
(e)	Any change in the named licensee may be permitted by the board of commissioners if the new named licensee meets the requirements of new license applicants. 
(f)	In the circumstances described in subsections (c), (d), and (e) of this section, the license may be revoked if the board of commissioners determines that the change results in a failure to meet the requirements of this chapter. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 10, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-111. - Change in business ownership. 
(a)	If any licensee withdraws from, sells, or otherwise transfers the licensee's interest in the licensed business, or ceases to operate the business continuously for a period of six months, the licensee shall immediately notify the county manager and surrender the license. 
(b)	In the case of such a withdrawal, transfer, or sale, a new application shall be made as for an original license. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 11, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-112. - Temporary licenses. 
(a)	A temporary license may be issued by the county manager while an application for a permanent license is pending, if in his judgment, the denial of a temporary license would create an undue hardship such as the closing of an existing business or a delay in the opening of a new business. 
(b)	A temporary license may be revoked, with or without cause, by the county manager at any time, and the grant or denial of a temporary license shall not affect or have any bearing upon the grant or denial of a permanent license. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 12, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-113. - Suspension, revocation. 
(a)	The violation of any of the provisions of this article shall be grounds for suspension or revocation of any license issued hereunder. 
(b)	Notwithstanding final disposition of a case by any court of competent jurisdiction, a license may be suspended or revoked by the board of commissioners for any violation of this article, for any violation of state or federal law, for any material misrepresentation or omission in the application for the license, or if the licensee or the licensed business ceases to meet the eligibility requirements for licensure. 
(c)	A law enforcement officer who determines that an emergency situation exists at any licensed premises which situation poses a significant threat to public safety, may immediately close the premises and take possession of the alcoholic beverage license and business license. Such licenses shall be delivered by the sheriff, along with an incident report, to the county manager or his designee within two business days who will determine if an emergency situation exists to authorize an emergency suspension as provided by subparagraph (d) hereof. 
(d)	The county manager is authorized to suspend the sale of alcoholic beverages under any license for any emergency situation that the county manager deems such suspension necessary for the protection of the public health, safety, or welfare. Such suspension may be made effective immediately and may remain in force until the county manager or chairman of the board of commissioners determines that the emergency is over or until the next meeting of the board of commissioners, at which time the suspension shall cease unless it is extended by the board of commissioners. Prior to suspending or revoking a license, except as noted in emergency situations in subsections (c) and (d) of this section, the board of commissioners shall give at least five days prior written notice to the licensee of the time, place, and purpose of the hearing at which such suspension or revocation will be considered. Service of such notice shall be perfected by personal service at the licensed premises on the named licensee or an employee of the licensee by a deputy sheriff; or, if personal service may not be so effected, by tacking a copy of the notice to the door of the licensed premises and mailing the original to the named licensee at the licensed premises with a copy mailed to any other address of the named licensee contained in the most recent license application on file with the county. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 13, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-114. - Automatic revocation. 
A license issued under this article shall be automatically revoked by operation of law if: 
(1)	The licensee's state alcoholic beverage license is revoked; 
(2)	Payment of the annual license fee is not received by the county within 14 days after notification that the issuance of a license has been approved by the board of commissioners; 
(3)	Operation of the licensed activity is not commenced within six months after the license is issued; 
(4)	Operation of the licensed activity is commenced and then discontinued for a period of 30 days unless extended by the board of commissioners for good cause; 
(5)	The licensed business declares bankruptcy or receivership, is the subject of levy or legal process, or fails to properly account for, file, report and pay any excise tax levied under this chapter; 
(6)	The licensed business fails to properly account for, file, report and maintain any records or remit any license fee imposed or taxes required under this chapter, including occupation taxes; 
Payment of the annual renewal license fee is not received by the county within the time prescribed in section 6-109; 
(7)	The named licensee is convicted of a felony, selling alcohol to minors, or a crime involving moral turpitude by a court of competent jurisdiction; 
(8)	Ad valorem taxes are not paid when due on the business or the premises within which the licensed business is operated. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 14, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-115. - Standard and guidelines for granting or denying licenses. 
In addition to all other requirements stated in this chapter, the board of commissioners shall consider the following standards and guidelines in reaching its decision on whether to grant or deny an application for a license allowing the sale of distilled spirits by the drink and for consumption on the premises: 
(1)	The nature of the neighborhood immediately adjacent to the proposed location, that is, whether the neighborhood is predominantly residential, industrial or business; 
(2)	The proximity of churches, schools, state licensed childcare centers, college campuses, housing authority properties, and alcoholic treatment centers owned and operated by the state or any county or municipal government therein, as required by section 6-109 of this chapter; 
(3)	The proximity of hospitals, public libraries, children's centers, public parks and playgrounds, and private residences; 
(4)	Whether the proposed location has adequate off-street parking facilities or other parking available for its patrons; 
(5)	Whether the location would tend to increase and promote traffic congestion and resulting hazards therefrom; 
(6)	The criminal record, general good character and reputation, and financial responsibility of the applicant and manager of the premises, provided that nonpayment of federal, state, county or municipal taxes shall be prima facie evidence of lack of financial responsibility; 
(7)	The report of the sheriff's department on its investigation and any other reports that may be required by the board of commissioners; 
(8)	Whether the applicant has satisfied all requirements pertaining to the application process and all requirements as to notice and advertisement; 
(9)	Consideration of the health, safety, and welfare of the citizens and preservation of surrounding neighborhoods, with reference to such factors as light, noise, pollution, traffic and loitering; 
(10)	The number of licenses already granted for similar businesses within the county limits and in the trading area of the location for which a license is sought; 
(11)	The history or reputation of the location for criminal activity, including but not limited to prostitution or other sex offenses, crimes of violence, gambling, and illegal dealing in alcoholic beverages or drugs; 
(12)	Any circumstance that may cause minors to frequent the immediate area, even if the location meets the distance requirements set forth in this chapter; and 
(13)	Whether the building meets the minimum standards of the latest edition of NFPA 101: Life Safety Code. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 15, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-116. - Decisions. 
All decisions approving, denying, suspending, or revoking the license required by this chapter shall be in writing, with the reasons therefore stated, and shall be mailed or delivered to the applicant. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 16, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-117. - Zoning restriction. 
No license shall be granted under this chapter unless the premises to be licensed are, at the time the application, approved by the board of commissioners, located under the planning and zoning ordinance of the county in a non-residential zoning district subject to the specific limitation of the respective districts. Any business currently possessing a license under this article is exempt from this section. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 17, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-118. - Proximity restrictions. 
(a)	No premises shall be licensed under this chapter whose location is within the following distances: 
(1)	Within 100 yards of any church grounds or 200 yards of a school building, school grounds, educational building, or college campus; or 
(2)	Within 100 yards of any alcoholic treatment center owned and operated by the State of Georgia or any county or municipal government therein. 
(b)	For the purpose of this section, distances shall be measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground from the front door of the licensed premises to the property line of the proscribed area. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 18, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-119. - Sale services in public places. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or serve any alcoholic beverage in a street, alley, or parking lot commonly used by the public or in any other public place or on public property unless otherwise approved in writing by the county commission. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 19, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-120. - Responsibility of named licensee. 
The named licensee shall be active in the operation of the licensed business and shall be personally present on the licensed premises sufficiently to assure compliance with the provisions of this chapter. The named licensee must maintain on the licensed premises phone numbers which will allow emergency contact with said licensee at all times. Failure of a licensee to identify themselves to law enforcement or be available by phone shall be a public safety violation which will authorize law enforcement to immediately close the premises pursuant to section 6-113(c). 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 20, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-121. - Rental paid restricted. 
Except as otherwise provided in this section, it shall be unlawful for a licensee to enter into any agreement whereby the rental paid for licensed premises is based in whole or in part on the volume of sales of alcoholic beverages by the licensed business or whereby the lessor otherwise shares in the profits or receipts from the licensed business' sale of alcoholic beverages. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 21, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-122. - Display of license. 
Each license issued under this article shall at all times be kept plainly exposed to public view and visible from the main entrance to the licensed premises. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 22, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-123. - Knowledge of article provisions. 
Every licensee under this article shall, prior to applying for a license, read and familiarize himself with the provisions of this article, and an application shall constitute a certification by the applicant that he has done so. Every licensee shall maintain a copy of this article on the licensed premises and shall instruct each employee engaged in the sale or handling of alcoholic beverages concerning the relevant provisions of the article. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 23, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-124. - Sales to underage persons prohibited. 
(a)	Except as otherwise provided in this section: 
(1)	No person, directly or through another person, shall furnish, cause to be furnished, or permit any person in such person's employ to furnish any alcoholic beverage to any person under 21 years of age. 
(2)	No person under 21 years of age shall purchase or possess any alcoholic beverage. 
(3)	No person under 21 years of age shall misrepresent such person's age in any manner whatever for the purpose of obtaining unlawfully any alcoholic beverage. 
(4)	No person shall act as an agent to purchase or acquire any alcoholic beverage for or on behalf of a person under 21 years of age. 
(5)	No person under 21 years of age shall misrepresent his identity or use any false identification for the purpose of purchasing or obtaining any alcoholic beverage. 
(b)	The prohibition contained in paragraph (1) of subsection (a) of this section shall not apply with respect to the sale of alcoholic beverages by a person when such person has been furnished with proper identification showing that the person to whom the alcoholic beverage is sold is 21 years of age or older. For purposes of this subsection, the term "proper identification" means any document issued by a governmental agency containing a description of the person, such person's photograph, or both, and giving such person's date of birth and includes, without being limited to, a passport, military identification, driver's license, or an identification card authorized by Georgia law. 
(c)	This section shall not prohibit employment of a person less than 21 years of age in licensed premises if such employment is lawful under section 6-129. 
(d)	In any case where a reasonable or prudent person could reasonably be in doubt as to whether or not the person to whom an alcoholic beverage is to be sold or otherwise furnished actually is 21 years of age or older, it shall be the duty of the person selling or otherwise furnishing such alcoholic beverage to request to see and be furnished with proper identification as provided in subsection (c) of this section in order to verify the age of such person; and the failure to make such request and verification in any case where the person to whom the alcoholic beverage is sold or otherwise furnished is less than 21 years of age may be considered by the trier of fact in determining whether the person selling or otherwise furnishing such alcoholic beverage did so in violation of paragraph (1) of subsection (a) of this section. 
(e)	In any case where a person selling or otherwise furnishing alcoholic beverages checks for a proper identification, such person shall carefully inspect such identification. If a reasonable and prudent person could determine that such identification has been altered and if such person sells or otherwise furnishes alcoholic beverages to the holder of such altered identification, then such may be considered by the trier of fact in determining whether the person selling or otherwise furnishing such alcoholic beverage did so in violation of paragraph (1) of subsection (a) of this section. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 24, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-125. - Days sales prohibited. 
(a)	No licensee shall permit the sale of distilled spirits by the drink on any day or any time when such sales are prohibited by state law. 
(b)	No licensee shall permit the sale or delivery of distilled spirits by the drink on Christmas Day. 
(c)	All licensees shall post the following notice: 
NOTICE 
It is a violation of the laws of the State of Georgia and the ordinances of the County of Upson to engage in the sale or delivery of distilled spirits by the drink on Sunday. 
Such notice shall be printed in black letters on a white background no smaller than 12 inches in length by 12 inches in height, and shall be prominently posted at the point of display. 
(d)	The sale of alcoholic beverages shall not be allowed on any election day during the hours that the polls are open. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 25, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-126. - Sales to intoxicated persons; gambling; disorderly conduct. 
(a)	No licensee shall permit the sale of alcoholic beverages to any person who is in a state of noticeable intoxication or allow persons who are noticeably intoxicated to congregate on licensed premises or any adjoining premises under the control of the licensee. 
(b)	No licensee shall permit any gambling, betting, illegal lottery, or other devise for the hazarding of any money or other known criminal activity or drug use on the licensed premises. 
(c)	No licensee shall permit on the licensed premises any disorderly conduct breach of the peace, or noise or activity which is disturbing to the surrounding neighborhood. 
(d)	No holder of a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages issued pursuant to the article shall knowingly allow any performance or entertainment or act on the licensed premises which, when applied to contemporary community standards, the dominant theme taken as a whole appeals to the prurient interests or is licentious or obscene. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 26, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-127. - Containers, storage, illumination. 
(a)	Alcoholic beverages shall be delivered to and received at licensed premises only in the original container and only in a conveyance owned and operated by a licensed wholesale dealer (or licensed common carrier acting for a wholesaler). Alcoholic beverages shall be sold at retail only on the licensed premises. 
(b)	A retail licensee shall store alcoholic beverages only on the licensed premises and at no other place. All stock shall be available at all times for inspection by any authorized agent of the county. Any alcoholic beverages found in any retail licensee's stock which were not received from a wholesaler licensed to make deliveries in the county shall be subject to immediate confiscation. 
(c)	The exterior of each building in which alcoholic beverages are sold for consumption on the premises shall contain sufficient lighting so that all sides of the building and all entrances thereto are clearly visible at all times. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 27, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-128. - Cleanliness of premises; inspections. 
All licensed premises shall be kept clean and in proper sanitary condition and in full compliance with all regulations governing the condition of premises used for the storage and sale of food for human consumption. All licensed premises shall be open at all times for inspection by authorized agents of the county. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 28, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-129. - Prohibited employment, exceptions. 
(a)	Except as provided in subsection (b) of this section, no licensee shall allow any employee under the age of 21 years to dispense, sell, serve, take orders for, or handle alcoholic beverages. 
(b)	This section shall not prohibit the employment of persons under the above ages on licensed premises, where such persons do not dispense, sell, serve, take orders for, or handle alcoholic beverages, except that no person under the age of 21 years shall be employed or present on the premises of a non-food service consumption on the premises licensee. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 29, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-130. - Employees restricted. 
No licensee shall knowingly employ on any licensed premises, in any capacity whatsoever any performers, dancers, entertainers, and musicians or other persons who have been convicted within the preceding ten years of any crime involving moral turpitude. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 30, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-131. - Consumption on the premises. 
(a)	Restaurant. In order to be eligible for a pouring consumption-on-the-premises license, a restaurant shall be defined as follows: 
(1)	Be used and held out to the public as a place where meals prepared on the premises are regularly served to the public for adequate pay each day the establishment is open for business; 
(2)	Contain one or more public dining rooms, with adequate and sanitary kitchen facilities and staff to prepare, cook and serve suitable food for its guests; 
(3)	Have staff available to serve meals prepared on the premises during any time the establishment is open for business; 
(4)	Have a valid county health department food service permit and any other applicable local, state or federal permits, licenses, etc., required for food service establishments; 
(5)	Have at least 50 percent of its total sales comprised of the sale of food prepared on the premises and nonalcoholic beverages consumed on the premises; and for this purpose, if a restaurant makes a minimum charge, cover charge, or admission charge, or any other nonfood or nonalcoholic beverage charge, the amount so charged shall not be counted in computing total sales and shall not be counted as a food or beverage sale; 
(6)	Have a permanent seating capacity, at tables, not counting bar stools, of at least 25 persons. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 31, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-132. - Noise control. 
A licensee of a consumption on the premises establishment shall at all times control the volume of music or other sounds originating within or from adjoining parking or other areas under the control of the licensee. A volume in excess of a normal conversational tone at the public roadway on which the licensed premises abuts shall be a violation of this section. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 32, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-133. - Statement of sales. 
All restaurant consumption on the premises licensees may be required to file with the county manager the following reports at the time and in the form prescribed by the county manager: 
(1)	Monthly on-premises consumption report. 
(2)	A certified copy of the licensee's monthly state sales tax report as filed with the state department of revenue for the period coinciding with on-premises consumption report. 
(3)	Any other documents, reports, records or books as shall be required by the county manager to insure compliance with license requirements. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 33, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-134. - Ratio of alcoholic, nonalcoholic sales. 
Should the total sales from food and nonalcoholic beverages reported by any licensee for a restaurant consumption on the premises not equal those form the sale of all alcoholic beverages for any two consecutive reporting periods, the license may be suspended or revoked by the board of commissioners after a hearing, as provided for in this article. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 34, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-135. - Illumination of premises, location of sales restricted. 
(a)	All restaurant and non-food service consumption on the premises areas, including all tables, booths, and other areas where customers are served and including all passageways for customers, shall be sufficiently well illuminated so that they may be viewed by those inside the premises. 
(b)	The sale of alcoholic beverages in any back room or side room, which is not open to the general public, is prohibited, expect that this prohibition shall not apply with respect to room service to hotel guests in their hotel rooms or banquet areas, provided a properly licensed restaurant is located on the premises. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 35, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-136. - Prohibited activities by employees. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any employee of a license holder to engage in the following: 
(1)	Dance or sit with customers on the premises while on duty status, including "breaks"; 
(2)	Allow any customer to purchase food or drink, alcoholic or nonalcoholic, for an employee while on duty status, including "break periods"; 
(3)	For an employee to consume or simulate the consumption of any alcoholic beverage while on duty status at the premises of his or her employer, including "breaks"; 
(4)	Require, permit, suffer, encourage or induce any employee or person to solicit at the licensed premises for himself or for any person other than the patron and guest of the patron, the purchase by the patron of any drink whether alcoholic or nonalcoholic; or money with which to purchase same; nor shall any licensee pay a commission or any other compensation to any person frequenting his establishment or to his agent or manager to solicit for himself, or for any other, the purchase by the patron of any drink, whether alcoholic or nonalcoholic. 
(b)	For purposes of this section the term "employee" shall also apply to performers, dancers entertainers, musicians engaged in temporary work, as well as regular employees. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 36, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-137. - Hours of sale. 
Consumption on the premises licensees may engage in the sale and service of alcoholic beverages only between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 1:30 a.m., Monday through Friday, between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 11:30 p.m., on Saturday. Alcoholic beverages purchased and served prior to 1:30 a.m., Monday through Friday, may be consumed on the premises until 2:00 a.m. Alcoholic beverages purchased and served prior to 11:30 p.m. on Saturday may be consumed on the premises until 12:00 midnight. Not later than 2:00 a.m., Monday through Friday and 12:00 midnight on Saturday the licensed premises must be closed to business and cleared of all patrons, both inside the premises and on any adjoining parking are or public property. No private after-hours party shall be permitted at licensed premises. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 37, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-138. - Dancing on premises restricted. 
Patron dancing shall be permitted at facilities licensed for consumption-on-the-premises sales only where: 
(1)	Adequate space exists; and 
(2)	All fire and safety regulations are met; 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 38, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-139. - Removal of beverages prohibited. 
All alcoholic beverages sold by consumption-on-the-premises licensees shall be consumed only on the licensed premises. It shall be unlawful for any person to remove from the licensed premises any alcoholic beverages sold for consumption on the premises. Each licensee shall be responsible for ensuring that no person so removes any alcoholic beverages from the premises in any type of container. 
(1)	Each consumption-on-the-premises licensee shall post in a prominent place at each exit from the licensed premises a sign in substantially the following form: 
"It is violation of County Ordinance to take any type alcoholic beverage from this outlet" 
Such sign shall be printed in uniform letters not less than one inch in height. 
(2)	It shall be unlawful for any person to drink or have in his possession an open container of any alcoholic beverage: 
a.	On any public street, sidewalk, park or other public place within the county, or upon or within any motor vehicle on the streets, sidewalks, parks and public places of the county; or 
b.	While on private property, open to public view, without the express permission of the owner, agent or person in lawful possession thereof. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 39, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-140. - Prohibited practices. 
(a)	No consumption-on-the-premises licensee shall engage in any of the following practices: 
(1)	The giving away of any alcoholic beverages in conjunction with the sale of any other alcoholic beverages; 
(2)	The sale of two or more alcoholic beverages for a single price or the sale of all the alcoholic beverages a customer can or desires to drink; 
(b)	Brown bag establishments as defined in this article shall be prohibited within the county. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 40, 2-23-2016) 
Sec. 6-141. - Excise tax. 
(a)	Tax imposed. There is an excise tax hereby imposed on the sale of distilled spirits in the maximum amount allowed by law, as now exists or hereafter amended. 
(1)	Said tax shall be paid to the board by each retailer on all distilled spirits sold within the incorporated areas of Upson County, Georgia, not later than the 10th of each month. The tax shall be based upon the retail price of all spirits sold during the previous calendar month by retailers in the said county. 
(2)	The retailer shall keep true and correct records of all sales and shall render a sworn statement of the same accompanying the monthly report and payment to the board. 
(3)	The board shall have the right to audit, and to require production of records form each retailer so supplied. 
(4)	Failure to make a timely report and remittance of aforesaid taxes shall render a wholesales dealer liable for a penalty equal to ten percent of the total amount due, in addition to the amount due; and additionally, if said report is not filed or if said taxes are not remitted and paid within 30 days from the date that the same are due, the board shall have the right to suspend and/or revoke any distilled spirits. 
(5)	It shall be unlawful for any person to sell retail or otherwise within the unincorporated areas of Upson County, Georgia any distilled spirits on which the tax required in this article has not been paid to the Board of Upson County, Georgia. 
(6)	All holders of alcohol beverage caterer's licenses shall be liable for collection and timely payments of all excise taxes due on sales at special event. Additionally, special event organizers should insure that all applicable sales tax is collected and remitted in such a way that Upson County benefits from taxes paid. 
( Ord. No. 245 , § 41, 2-23-2016) 
Secs. 6-142—6-160. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE SPECIAL EVENT PERMIT 

Sec. 6-161. - Title. 
This article shall be known as and may be cited as the "Alcoholic Beverage Special Event Permit." 
( Ord. No. 246 , § 1, 3-22-2016) 
Sec. 6-162. - Authority and jurisdiction. 
Whereas, consistent with Georgia Law, the Upson County Board of Commissioners has the authority to establish by ordinance or resolution such local rules and regulations, not in conflict with existing state or federal law, relating to the health, safety, and welfare of the public. 
Now therefore be it resolved that the following rules and regulations are hereby adopted. These regulations shall apply to all unincorporated land located within the boundaries of Upson County, Georgia. 
The purpose for the enactment of this article is to establish a special event permit authorizing the sale of wine and/or beer and malt beverages and/or distilled spirits for consumption on the premise of a permitted location not to exceed a three-day period. 
( Ord. No. 246 , § 1, 3-22-2016) 
Sec. 6-163. - Alcoholic beverage special event permit. 
A special event shall be defined as an organized activity having as its purpose entertainment, recreation and/or education which takes place on private or public property. Such special events may include but are not limited to the following: fairs, tours, grand openings, races, parades, marches, rallies, assemblies, festivals, concerts, and holiday celebrations. A special event permit is required for all special events that involve the consumption of alcohol. 
( Ord. No. 246 , § 2, 3-22-2016) 
Sec. 6-164. - Special event permit requirements. 
(a)	Except as provided for in section 6-166 of this article, wine and/or beer and malt beverages and/or distilled spirits shall only be sold, served, or otherwise provided at a special event only if the person providing said alcoholic beverage has applied for and received a special event permit. 
(b)	In order to sell, serve, or otherwise provide wine, and/or beer and malt beverages, and/or distilled spirits at a special event, at a permitted location, the person providing, wine and/or beer and malt beverages and/or distilled spirits at a special event shall be required to comply with the following: 
(1)	Complete an application form with the board of county commissioners as provided by the county. 
(2)	All applications must be completed in full and submitted at least 14 days prior to the planned special event. Upon a showing of good cause, any application filed less than 14 days before the special event may be consider and approved at the discretion of the county manager, or his designee, and be subject to a $200.00 late fee. 
(3)	Applicants must be at least 21 years of age, a United States citizen or an alien lawfully admitted for permanent residency, and a resident of the State of Georgia. 
(4)	If the applicant is not the owner as listed on the deed of the property wherein said wine and/or beer and malt beverages and/or distilled spirits shall be served, a notarized letter from the property owner, including phone number and address, authorizing the applicant to act on their behalf must be provided at the time the application is considered. 
(5)	All applications will be considered for approval by the county manager or his designee. If the county manager or designee finds the application is deficient and therefore denied, applicants may appeal in writing to the board of commissioners within five days of the date of the denial. Any appeal received outside of the five-day deadline will not be considered. 
(6)	Prior to receiving a permit, each applicant must have security measures in place approved by the sheriff concerning noise control, crowd control, traffic and compliance with all local, state, and federal laws. 
(7)	For all approved applications, applicants will receive a permit from the office of the board of commissioners. All permits must be made available on site when requested by any county, state, or federal official. 
(8)	Each application shall specify the date, time and location of the event and may not be changed except by approval of the county manager or his designee. 
(9)	Incomplete applications shall not be considered for approval. 
(10)	Applicants must pay a $100.00 application fee for each special event permit to the office of the board of commissioners. This application fee shall be non-refundable. Each applicant shall be liable for any additional costs incurred by the county as a result of the event. 
(11)	Permits approved by the county shall authorize the applicant to sell wine and/or beer and malt beverages and/or distilled spirits for consumption on the premise of the permitted location for a period not to exceed three days, subject to all laws and ordinances regulating the selling of such beverages; no more than six such permits may be issued to the applicant in any one calendar year. 
(12)	All event locations and all applicants must otherwise be in compliance with all federal, state, and local law. 
(13)	All event locations must comply with current zoning ordinances of Upson County subject to the specific limitations of the respective districts. For alcoholic beverage special event permitting purposes only, a special event license may be granted for locations zoned A-R (agricultural residential). 
( Ord. No. 246 , § 2, 3-22-2016) 
Sec. 6-165. - Payment of taxes and other county debt. 
The county manager or his designee shall be authorized to cause an inquiry into the tax records of any applicant or other interested party to an application to determine if any outstanding taxes, special assessments, unpaid utilities or any other monies are owed to the county. No permit shall be considered for issuance whereby it is determined there are outstanding monies owed to the county. 
( Ord. No. 246 , § 3, 3-22-2016) 
Sec. 6-166. - Exceptions. 
The requirements of this chapter shall not apply to a private function held at a private residence at which alcoholic beverages are purchased and served by a person not otherwise required to be licensed pursuant to this or any other ordinance to invited guests of such person, provided that the person holding the event purchases the alcoholic beverage and receives no payment of any kind from the invited guests, and the event is not open or accessible to the general public and is otherwise permitted under the county's ordinances. 
( Ord. No. 246 , § 4, 3-22-2016) 
Sec. 6-167. - Violations; penalties; revocations. 
(a)	No person shall violate any of the provisions of this article or assist another in evading the requirements imposed by this article. Any person who shall violate this article shall, upon conviction, be subject to the punishment as provided in section 1-11. 
(b)	The county manager or county clerk shall have the authority to revoke a special events permit issued under this article upon a finding that the application as filed contained false, misleading, or incomplete information and therefore does not comply with the standards for issuance as set forth under this article. 
( Ord. No. 246 , § 5, 3-22-2016) 
Chapter 10 - AMUSEMENTS AND ENTERTAINMENTS[1]
