DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 187, § 1, adopted November 12, 2006, repealed the former division 1, §§ 22-31—22-34, and enacted a new division 1 as set out herein. The former division 1 pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Ord. No. 63, adopted September 19, 1991. 

Sec. 22-31. - Interpretation of chapter. 
This chapter shall be deemed an exercise of the police powers of the county for the preservation and protection of the public health, peace, safety and welfare, and all its provisions shall be liberally construed for that purpose. This chapter shall be construed together with the other provisions of this Code and other ordinances of the county relating to the construction and use of buildings and structures, and in the event of the conflicts with those provisions or ordinances, the provision deemed to achieve the greatest promotion of the public welfare shall be deemed controlling. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 1, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 22-32. - Penalties for violations. 
Any person convicted in the magistrate court of the violation of any of the terms of this chapter or the codes adopted hereby shall be punished as provided in section 1-11 of this Code. Each day that a violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 1, 12-12-2006) 
Secs. 22-33—22-60. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ADOPTION[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 187, § 2, adopted November 12, 2006, repealed the former division 2, §§ 22-61, and enacted a new division 2 as set out herein. The former division 2 pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Ord. No. 63, adopted September 19, 1991. 

Sec. 22-61. - Technical building and construction codes adopted. 
(a)	The following technical building and construction codes are adopted by reference and may be amended for later editions as required by the Georgia Uniform Codes Act, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-25: 
(1)	International Building Code (SBCCI), 2006 Edition, including Appendices A through J, M, N, P, Q, R and S; 
(2)	International Plumbing Code (SBCCI), 2006 Edition; 
(3)	International Mechanical Code (SBCCI), 2006 Edition; 
(4)	International Gas Code (SBCCI), 2000 Edition; 
(5)	International Fire Prevention Code (SBCCI), 2006 Edition; 
(6)	National Electrical Code with Georgia Amendments as published by the National Fire Protection Association (NFPA), 2005 Edition; 
(7)	Council of American Building Officials (CABO) One- and Two-Family Dwelling Code with Georgia Amendments, 2000 Edition; 
(8)	Council of American Building Officials (CABO) Model Energy Code with Georgia Amendments, 1995 Edition; 
(9)	International Fuel Gas Code, 2006 Edition; 
(10)	International Energy Conservation Code, 2000 Edition; 
(11)	International Residential Code, 2006 Edition. 
(b)	In addition, the following optional codes are also adopted by reference as though they were copied herein fully: 
(1)	International Existing Buildings Code (SBCCI), 2003 Edition; 
(2)	Standard Housing Code (SBCCI) with Georgia amendments, 1994 Edition; 
(3)	Standard Unsafe Building Abatement Code (SBCCI), 1985 Edition; 
(4)	Standard Swimming Pool Code with Georgia amendments, 1994 Edition; 
(5)	Standard Amusement Device Code, 1985 Edition; 
(6)	Standard Excavation and Grading Code, 1975 Edition. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 2, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 22-62. - Officials. 
When reference is made in the technical codes adopted by this chapter to the duties of certain officials named therein, then the designated official of the county who has duties corresponding to those of the named official in such codes shall be deemed to be the responsible official insofar as enforcing the provisions of such codes are concerned. The term "governing body" or "applicable governing body" as used in any of these codes shall refer in each instance to the board of commissioners of Upson County. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 2, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 22-63. - Copies available; maintenance. 
The copy of the codes and amendments adopted under this chapter and filed with the office of the county manager shall be county property and shall be preserved by the county manager and the county clerk and maintained in a manner convenient for public examination and use and shall be open to public examination and use in the office of the county clerk during regular business hours, but shall not be taken out of the office for any reason except for use in a trial of an issue related to the terms of this chapter, before the magistrate court, the zoning board of appeals or the courts of the state. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 2, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 22-64. - Fees. 
(a)	Schedule of building permit fees. 
(1)	Residential building permit fees are based on construction cost of $90.00 per square foot for heated living area, $35.00 per square foot for garage, and $30.00 per square foot for unfinished basement, porch, terrace, and carport area. Total valuation fees as follows: 
a.	Two thousand dollars and less: No fees, unless inspection required, in which case a $25.00 fee for each inspection shall be charged; 
b.	Two thousand one dollars to $50,000.00: Twenty dollars for the first $1,000.00 plus $5.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof, to and including $50,000.00; 
c.	Fifty thousand one dollars to $100,000.00: Two hundred sixty-four dollars for the first $50,000.00 plus $4.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof, to and including $99,000.00; 
d.	One hundred thousand dollars to $500,000.00: Four hundred sixty-five dollars for the first $100,000.00 plus $3.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof, to and including $500,000.00; 
e.	Five hundred thousand one dollars and up: One thousand six hundred sixty dollars for the first $500,000.00 plus $2.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof. 
(2)	Commercial/industrial building permit fees are based on construction cost of $85.00 per square foot. Total valuation fees as follows: 
a.	Five hundred dollars to $3,000.00: Fifty dollars; 
b.	Three thousand one dollars $50,000.00: Fifty dollars for the first $3,000.00 plus $6.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof, to and including $50,000.00; 
c.	Fifty thousand one dollars to $100,000.00: Three hundred thirty-two dollars for the first $50,000.00 plus $5.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof, to and including $100,000.00; 
d.	One hundred thousand one dollars to $500,000.00: Five hundred eighty-two dollars for the first $100,000.00 plus $4.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof, to and including $500,000.00; 
e.	Five hundred thousand one dollars and up: Two thousand one hundred eighty-two dollars for the first $500,000.00 plus $3.00 for each additional thousand or fraction thereof. 
(b)	Re-inspection fee for permitted jobs. After an inspection is requested, if the work is disapproved by the building inspector or if the building is not ready for inspection when the inspector arrives, a $35.00 re-inspection fee will be required to be paid prior to a re-inspection being made. If a second re-inspection is required, the fee will be $50.00 and the re-inspection fee will be required to be paid prior to the second re-inspection being made. If a third re-inspection is required, the fee will be $75.00 and the re-inspection fee will be required to be paid prior to the third re-inspection being made. Any further re-inspections after the third will be $100.00 each. All re-inspection fees must be paid before further inspections or new inspections are performed and before any certificate of occupancy is issued. 
(c)	Miscellaneous construction permit/moving fee. For the moving of any structure, the fee shall be $100.00. These fees shall be paid by property owner not the tenant. 
(d)	Demolition fee. Fee shall be one percent of the accessed value of the property being demolished with a minimum fee of $50.00. 
(e)	Penalties. Where work for which a permit is required is started or proceeded prior to obtaining said permit, the fee herein specified shall be doubled. The payment of such double fee shall not relieve any person from fully complying with the requirements of applicable codes in the execution of the work, nor from any other penalties prescribed herein. 
(f)	Plan-checking fee. When the valuation of construction exceeds $2,000.00, a plan is required to be submitted in compliance with chapter 105.3 of Standard Building Code (SBCCI), a plan-check fee shall be paid to the building official at the time of submitting the plan and specifications for checking. The amount of the plan-check fee shall be equal to one-half of the building permit fee as set forth herein. Such plan-check fee is in addition to the building permit fee. 
(g)	Calculation of electrical permit fees: 
(1)	Residential. Forty-five dollars for the first 200 amp service, plus $15.00 for each additional 200 amps or fraction thereof. 
(2)	Commercial and industrial. Fifty-five dollars for the first 200 amp service, plus $25.00 for each additional 200 amps or fraction thereof. 
(h)	Calculation of plumbing permit fees: 
(1)	Residential. Forty-five dollars for the first 12 fixtures or traps plus $5.00 for each additional fixture or trap thereafter. 
(2)	Commercial and industrial. Fifty-five dollars initial fee for issuing each permit, plus $5.00 for each fixture or trap. 
(i)	Calculation of heating and air conditioning permit fees: 
(1)	Residential. Forty-five dollars for the first 100,000 BTU and/or five-ton heat-pump, plus $20.00 for each additional 50,000 BTU and/or three-ton heat-pump or fraction thereof. 
(2)	Commercial and industrial. Fifty-five dollars initial fee for issuing each permit, plus $5.00 for each additional $1,000.00 or fraction thereof, of valuation of the installation. 
(j)	Contractor and subcontractor license fees. The contractor and subcontractor license fees will be established in accordance with the policies set forth in the county's occupation tax ordinance. 
(k)	Exceptions to fee schedule. The fees specified herein shall apply to any person, firm, or corporation, except as follows: 
(1)	The fees shall be waived for permits to repair or rebuild property damaged by storms, tornadoes, snow, hail, wind or other natural disasters. Such disaster must be verified by the building inspector. Applicable permits must be obtained, but at no charge. 
(2)	All projects financed by federal, state, county and city funds are exempt from permit fees. Applicable permits must be obtained, but at no charge. 
(l)	Blasting permits must be obtained in accordance with the requirements of Georgia Law and a copy of any permits obtained must be filed with the county building inspector. 
(m)	Residential home sale and rental inspection fee. There shall be no charge for the initial inspection and the first follow-up inspection. There shall be a $50.00 fee for the second follow-up inspection. There shall be a $75.00 fee for the third follow-up inspection. There shall be a $100.00 fee for the fourth follow-up inspection and each additional inspection thereafter. All fees must be paid before the inspections are made. This inspection is good for two years and the property does not have to be re-inspected within said period even if the property is sold. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 2, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 199, §§ 1—4, 12-11-2007; Ord. No. 201, § 1, 12-13-2007) 
Sec. 22-65. - Violations; presumption violator is owner. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to violate the provisions of this chapter or the terms and standards adopted by reference thereby, to permit or maintain such violation, to refuse to obey any provision thereof, or to fail or refuse to comply with any provision or regulation except as variation may be allowed by action of the zoning board of appeals in writing. Proof of such unlawful act or failure to act or failure to comply shall be deemed prima facie evidence that such act or omission is the act of the owner of the property. Prosecution, or lack thereof, of either the owner or the occupant shall not be deemed to relieve the other. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 2, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 22-66. - Enforcement; interpretations of rules; request for variance. 
The building inspector shall have the responsibility for making interpretations of the rules adopted by this chapter, and for deciding upon the approval of equipment and materials, and for the granting of the special permission contemplated in a number of the rules. Any person aggrieved by the rulings of the building inspector with respect to this chapter may appeal as provided in sections 22-151—22-155. In conducting inspections of buildings, the building inspector shall apply the standards adopted by this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 2, 12-12-2006) 
Sec. 22-67. - Noncompliance; notice of violation; appeals; order to vacate. 
In the event that the building inspector shall find deviations from or noncompliance with the terms and standards adopted by this chapter, he may issue a written notice of violation, which shall be posted on the premises, and copy of which shall be mailed to the last known address of the owner of the premises. An appeal from the notice of violation may be made in a request for variance to the zoning board of appeals within 30 days of the date of issuance. Notice of violation may, in the event the building inspector determines that there is a clear, present, immediate and dangerous hazardous condition, dangerous to life, include an order to vacate the premises, and noncompliance with such an order shall be a violation of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 2, 12-12-2006) 
Secs. 22-68—22-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - AMENDMENTS 

Sec. 22-91. - Standard Building Code. 
(a)	The Standard Building Code adopted in section 22-61 is amended as follows: 
Sections 301.2, 301.2.1 and 301.2.2 are deleted and the following is substituted in lieu thereof: 
301.2. For the purpose of this code the term "fire district" shall be construed to mean all areas within the unincorporated confines of Upson County, Georgia. 
Section A101.4.1 is deleted and there is substituted in lieu thereof the following: 
(b) The building official shall have had such experience in the building industry as in the opinion of the chief appointing authority qualifies him to assume the responsibility of his office. He shall be appointed by the chief appointing authority of the county; his appointment shall continue during good behavior and satisfactory service. He shall not be removed from office except for cause, after full opportunity has been given him to be heard on specific charges before such chief appointing authority. 
Sections A105.4.1 and A105.4.2 are deleted and there is substituted in lieu thereof the following: 
A105.4.1. There is hereby established a board to be called the board of adjustments and appeals, which shall consist of five members. Said board members shall have such qualifications as shall be determined by the chief appointing authority, and shall serve for such times and at the sole discretion of said chief appointing authority. A quorum for said board shall consist of three members. A majority vote of said three members shall be sufficient to carry out any business or determine any appeal which it is authorized to hear. 
(b)	Notwithstanding any other provision of such code: 
(1)	Subfloors may not be built using particle board nor may particle board be used as underlayment in the kitchen, bathroom, laundry, or other wet areas. 
(2)	Roofs may not have more than three layers of shingles, including wooden shingles. 
(c)	Notwithstanding any provision to the contrary contained in any of the codes which have been adopted by reference in section 22-61, any decision by the building official or any assistant of his, under any of such codes, may be appealed by the aggrieved party to the board of adjustments and appeals created pursuant to the provisions of section A105.4.1 of the Standard Building Code, as amended in this section, and the terms and provisions of sections A105.4.3, A105.4.4 and A105.4.5 shall control such appeal. 
(Ord. No. 63, §§ 3(A), 14, 15, 9-19-1991) 
Sec. 22-92. - Standard Plumbing Code. 
The Standard Plumbing Code, adopted in section 22-61, is amended as follows: 
(1)	Notwithstanding any provision contained in the Standard Plumbing Code, the board of commissioners shall have full discretion as to whether or not to allow anyone to tap into the county sewer system. If allowed, the cost for such tap shall be as follows: 
a.	For a single tap for a subdivision or multifamily dwelling, the cost shall be based on total man hours at the man's actual pay plus materials, including all reasonable costs incurred by the county. 
b.	For a single tap at a single-family dwelling, the cost shall be as provided in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners, unless total man hours plus cost of materials exceeds such sum, in which case the cost shall be total man hours at the man's regular pay, plus materials including all reasonable costs incurred by the county. 
(2)	The property owner is responsible for bringing the tap line to his property line. 
(Ord. No. 63, § 3(B), 9-19-1991) 
Sec. 22-93. - National Electrical Code. 
(a)	The National Electrical Code, adopted in section 22-61, is amended as follows: 
Article 230-90(a), exception no. 3 is deleted in its entirety. 
Article 310-5 is amended so that conductors, whether solid or stranded, shall not be smaller than no. 12. Structures which require branch circuits to be installed within that structure, those circuits (located on the load side of the main breaker) shall be wired in copper except for all 220 volt circuits, other than window air conditioning units. Aluminum conductors where allowed shall be no smaller than 6. 
(b)	The code is further amended as follows: 
(1)	The electrical service including the main breaker box for all structures shall be a minimum of 100 amperes; 
(2)	The electric service entrance installed in any building shall be at least 100 amperes per building unit, except that in a multiunit residential apartment building with a central laundry room, the electric service entrance may be 60 amperes per residential unit; and 
(3)	The ground wire shall be a minimum of no. 6 on 100 amperes service, a minimum of no. 4 on 150 amperes and 200 amperes service. 
(Ord. No. 63, §§ 4, 17, 9-19-1991) 
Sec. 22-94. - Standard Fire Prevention Code. 
The Standard Fire Prevention Code, adopted in section 22-61, is amended as follows: 
Section 1.04 is amended by adding to the end thereof an additional sentence to read as follows: 
Whenever in this Fire Prevention Code the term "fire official," "chief of the fire department" or "chief of the bureau of fire prevention" is used, each of said terms shall be deemed and construed to mean the building official, or his assistant, which office is created by section 101.4 of the Standard Building Code. 
(Ord. No. 63, § 5, 9-19-1991) 
Sec. 22-95. - Standard Unsafe Building Abatement Code. 
The Standard Unsafe Building Abatement Code, as adopted in section 22-61, is amended as follows: 
Section 102.1. Organization, is amended as follows: 
Enforcement officer shall be amended to read as follows: 
The provisions of this code shall be enforced by the building official who shall be primarily responsible for its enforcement. The provisions of this code may also be enforced by the Upson County Code Enforcement Officer, under the supervision of the building official or such other persons as may be designated by the board of commissioners. 
Section 202. Definitions, is amended as follows: 
Applicable governing body shall mean the board of commissioners of Upson County, Georgia. 
Building official shall mean the building inspector of Upson County or his duly authorized representative. 
Department shall mean the building and zoning department of Upson County, Georgia. 
Office of the recorder shall mean the clerk of the superior court of Upson County, Georgia. 
Section 502.1. Filing, is amended as follows: 
The board or hearing examiner may obtain the issuance and service of subpoenas for the attendance of witnesses or the production of evidence at the hearings. Subpoenas may be issued upon the request of any member of the board, the hearing examiner, or upon the written request of any party involved in the hearing. The clerk of the board of commissioners of Upson County shall issue subpoenas and the sheriff of Upson County or the magistrate court constable shall serve the subpoenas all in accordance with the laws of the State of Georgia. 
Section 505. Recourse, is amended as follows: 
If the appellant is aggrieved by the decision of the board of adjustments and appeals, then he may appeal said decision de novo to the superior court of Upson County, Georgia. Said appeal must be filed within 15 days from the effective date of the board's final decision. Any appeal filed later than 15 days from the effective date of the board's final decision shall not be timely filed and shall be dismissed. 
Section 601.2.2 is amended as follows: 
Subsequent to posting the building, the building official may cause the building to be repaired to the extent required to render it safe or, if the notice requires demolition, to cause the building or structure to be demolished and all debris removed from the premises. The cost of repair or demolition shall constitute a lien on the property and shall be collected in the manner provided by chapter 7, as amended, of the Standard Unsafe Building Abatement Code of Upson County. 
Chapter 7, Recovery of Cost of Repair or Demolition, is stricken in its entirety and inserted in lieu thereof is a new chapter 7 to read as follows: 
701.1 That the amount of the cost incurred by, or at the direction of, the building official to repair or demolish the dwelling, building, or structure shall be a lien against the real property upon which such costs were incurred. Said lien shall attach to the real property upon the payment of all costs of repairing or demolition by the county and the filing of an itemized statement of the total sum of said costs by the building official in the office of the clerk of the superior court of Upson County in the lien docket maintained by said clerk for such purposes. If the dwelling, building, or structure is demolished by the building official, then said official shall sell the materials of such dwelling, building, or structure and shall credit the proceeds of such sale against the cost of the demolition, and any balance remaining shall be deposited in the superior court by the building official; such amount shall be secured in such manner as may be directed by the court, and shall be disbursed by such court to persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of said court. Nothing in this paragraph shall be construed to impair or limit in any way the power of the county to define and declare nuisances and to cause their removal or abatement by summary proceedings or otherwise. 
701.2 The collection of any amount due on such lien for the demolition for dwellings, buildings, or structures as set forth in paragraph 701.1 above shall be enforced in the following manner: 
(1)	The owner or parties at interest shall be allowed to satisfy the amount due on such lien by paying to the county, within 30 days after the perfection of said lien, a sum of money equal to 25 percent of the total amount due and by further paying to the county the remaining balance due on such lien, together with interest at the rate of seven percent per annum, in three equal annual payments, each of which shall become due and payable on the anniversary date of the initial payment made as set forth in this paragraph. 
(2)	Should the property upon which such lien is perfected be sold, transferred, or conveyed by the owner or parties at interest at any time prior to the termination of said three-year period, then the entire balance due on such lien shall be due and payable to the county upon the occurrence of such sale, transfer, or conveyance. 
(3)	Should the amount due on such lien, or any portion thereof, be unpaid after the passage of said three-year period, or upon the occurrence of the contingency provided for in subparagraph (2) above, or the failure of the owner to make the payments in a timely fashion as set out in subparagraph (1) above, then and in such event, the county may enforce the collection of any amount due on such lien for repair or demolition of dwellings, buildings, or structures in the same manner as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-4-1 et seq. and other applicable state statutes. This procedure shall be subject to the right of redemption by any person having any right, title, interest, or lien in or upon said property, as in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-4-3 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 63, § 9, 9-19-1991; Ord. No. 139, § 1, 10-18-2000) 
Secs. 22-96—22-120. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - PERMIT FEES 

Sec. 22-121. - Established. 
The permits required to be obtained by virtue of the provisions of any of the codes which have been adopted by, and incorporated by reference in section 22-61 shall, notwithstanding any provision contained in any of such codes thus adopted by reference, not be issued until the fees provided for in this division shall have been paid, which fees are hereby established for the following categories and set forth in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners: 
(1)	Total cost of the proposed work. 
(2)	Moving building or structure. 
(3)	Demolition of building or structure. 
(4)	Electrical wiring, additions or repair, in existing structures, of less than $2,001.00. 
(5)	Installation of exterior signs. 
(6)	Replacement or addition of heating and/or central air conditioning units. 
(Ord. No. 63, § 13(A)—(F), 9-19-1991) 
Sec. 22-122. - Plan checking fees. 
When the valuation of the proposed construction exceeds $1,000.00 and a plan is required to be submitted by section 105.3 of the Standard Building Code adopted in section 22-61, a plan checking fee shall be paid to the building official at the time of submitting plans and specifications for checking. The plan checking fee shall be equal to one-half of the building permit fee as set forth in section 22-121. The fee paid under this section shall be credited to any fee that becomes due under section 22-121(1). 
(Ord. No. 63, § 13(H), 9-19-1991) 
Sec. 22-123. - Applicability. 
The fees set out in section 22-121(1) shall apply to permits required to be obtained by virtue of the provisions of any of the standard published codes adopted by reference in section 22-61, but the costs of any portion of the work shall be counted only once in determining the amount of the required fee regardless of the fact that such work might otherwise be subject to a fee under more than one of such adopted codes. Notwithstanding any other section of this article or any provision of any of such standard codes which may provide to the contrary, the contractor with the ultimate responsibility for the work shall obtain the permit and pay the fee required under this division for the work, regardless of the fact that a subcontractor may actually perform the work. 
(Ord. No. 63, § 13(I), 9-19-1991) 
Sec. 22-124. - Failure to obtain permit. 
Where work for which a permit as required by this article is started or proceeded with prior to obtaining the required permit, the fees specified shall, as an administrative penalty, be doubled, but the payment of such double fee shall not relieve any person from complying with the requirements of this article in the execution of the work nor from any other penalties prescribed in this article. 
(Ord. No. 63, § 13(G), 9-19-1991) 
Secs. 22-125—22-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - BOARD OF ADJUSTMENTS AND APPEALS[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2. 

Sec. 22-151. - Created; powers. 
There is hereby created the Upson County Board of Adjustments and Appeals, referred to in this article as the "board of adjustments and appeals" to have and exercise the power to: 
(1)	Hear and decide appeals from any order, requirement, decision, or determination made by the building official in the enforcement of article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter; 
(2)	Hear and decide special exceptions to the terms of article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter upon which such board of adjustments and appeals under such regulations may be required to pass; and 
(3)	Hear and decide specific variances. 
(Ord. No. 56, § X(1), 9-21-1990) 
Sec. 22-152. - Composition; terms. 
(a)	The board of adjustments and appeals shall consist of five members approved by the county commission. 
(b)	Each member shall serve for a term of three years and until his successor is duly appointed and qualified. 
(Ord. No. 56, § X(2), 9-21-1990) 
Sec. 22-153. - Rules of procedure. 
(a)	The board of adjustments and appeals shall adopt rules for its governance and in harmony with article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter. Meetings of the board of adjustments and appeals shall be held at the call of the chairman and at such other times as the board may determine. The chairman or, in his absence, the acting chairman may administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses. All hearings of the board of adjustments and appeals shall be public. The board of adjustments and appeals shall keep minutes of its proceedings showing the vote of each member upon each question or, if absent or failing to vote, indicating such fact and shall keep records of its examinations and other official actions, all of which shall immediately be filed in the office of building official and on due cause shown. 
(b)	The board of adjustments and appeals shall make written findings of facts and conclusions of law giving the facts upon which it acted and its legal conclusions from such facts in reversing, affirming, or modifying any order, requirement, decision, or determination which comes before it under article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter. 
(c)	The concurring vote of a majority of the members of the board of adjustments and appeals shall be sufficient to reverse any order, requirement, decision, or determination of the building official or to decide in favor of the applicant on any matter upon which it is required to pass under article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter or to effect variation in article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 56, § X(3)—(5), 9-21-1990) 
Sec. 22-154. - Appeals. 
(a)	Any person aggrieved or any taxpayer affected by any decision of the building official made in his administration of article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter may appeal to the board of adjustments and appeals. 
(b)	All such appeals must be taken within a reasonable time as provided by the rules of the board of adjustments and appeals by filing with the building official a notice of appeal specifying the grounds thereof. The building official shall forthwith transmit to the board of adjustments and appeals all the papers constituting the record upon which the action appealed from was taken. 
(c)	An appeal shall stay all proceedings in furtherance of the action appealed from unless the building official certifies to the board of adjustments and appeals, after the notice of appeal has been filed with it, that because of the facts stated in the certificate a stay would, in his opinion, cause imminent peril to life or property. In such case, proceedings shall not be stayed except by order of the board of adjustments and appeals on notice to the building official and on due cause shown. 
(d)	The board of adjustments and appeals shall fix a reasonable time for hearing appeals, shall give public notice and due notice to the parties in interest, and shall decide the appeal within a reasonable time. Upon the hearing, any party may appear in person or by agent or by attorney. 
(e)	The board of adjustments and appeals may, in conformity with article II of chapter 18 and article II of this chapter, reverse or affirm, in whole or in part, or modify the order, requirement, decision, or determination appealed from and may make such order, requirement, decision, or determination as may be appropriate under the circumstances. 
(Ord. No. 56, § XI, 9-21-1990) 
Sec. 22-155. - Judicial review. 
Every decision of the board of adjustments and appeals shall be final, subject however to such remedy as any aggrieved party might argue as a point of law to the Upson Superior Court. 
(Ord. No. 56, § XII, 9-21-1990) 
Secs. 22-156—22-180. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - FLOW-RATE RESTRICTIONS ON PLUMBING FIXTURES[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
State Law reference— Flow-rate restrictions on plumbing fixtures, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-3. 

Sec. 22-181. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commercial means any type of building other than residential. 
Construction means the erection of a new building or the alteration of an existing building in connection with its repair or renovation or in connection with making an addition to an existing building and includes the replacement of a malfunctioning, unserviceable, or obsolete faucet, showerhead, toilet or urinal in an existing building. 
Residential means any building or unit of a building intended for occupancy as a dwelling but does not include a hotel or motel. 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 22-182. - Enforcement; penalty for violation. 
(a)	This article shall be enforced by the county building official, and citations for violations shall be issued by the building official. 
(b)	Any person violating this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
Sec. 22-183. - Residential construction. 
On or after July 1, 1991, no construction may be initiated within the unincorporated area of the county for any residential building of any type which employs: 
(1)	A gravity tank-type, flushometer-valve, or flushometer-tank toilet that uses more than an average of 1.6 gallons of water per flush; provided, however, this subsection shall not be applicable to one-piece toilets until July 1, 1992; 
(2)	A showerhead that allows a flow of more than an average of 2.5 gallons of water per minute at 60 pounds of pressure per square inch; 
(3)	A urinal that uses more than an average of one gallon of water per flush; 
(4)	A lavatory faucet or lavatory replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than two gallons of water per minute; or 
(5)	A kitchen replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2.5 gallons of water per minute. 
Sec. 22-184. - Commercial construction. 
On and after July 1, 1992, there shall be no construction initiated within the unincorporated area of the county for any commercial building of any type which does not meet the requirements of section 22-183. 
Sec. 22-185. - Repairs, renovations and additions. 
The requirements of section 22-183 shall apply to any residential construction initiated after July 1, 1991, and to any commercial construction initiated after July 1, 1992, which involves the repair or renovation of or addition to any existing building when such repair or renovation of or addition to such building includes replacement of toilets or showers or both. 
Sec. 22-186. - Exemptions. 
(a)	New construction and the repair or renovation of an existing building shall be exempt from the requirements of sections 22-183, 22-184 and 22-185 when: 
(1)	The repair or renovation of the existing building does not include the replacement of the plumbing or sewage system servicing toilets, faucets or showerheads within such existing building; 
(2)	Such plumbing or sewage system within such existing building, because of its capacity, design, or installation, would not function properly if the toilets, faucets or showerheads required by this article were installed; 
(3)	Such system is a well or gravity flow from a spring and is owned privately by an individual for use in such individual's personal residence; or 
(4)	Units to be installed are: 
a.	Specifically designed for use by the handicapped; 
b.	Specifically designed to withstand unusual abuse or installation in a penal institution; or 
c.	Toilets for juveniles. 
(b)	The owner or his agent of a building undergoing new construction or repair or renovation who is entitled to an exemption as specified in subsection (a)(2), (3) or (4) of this section shall obtain the exemption by applying at the office of the county building official. A fee as provided in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners shall be charged for the inspection and issuance of such exemption. 
Sec. 22-187. - Limitations. 
This article shall not apply to any construction of a residential building, the contract for which was entered into prior to July 1, 1991, and shall not apply to any construction of a commercial building, the contract for which was entered into prior to July 1, 1992. 
Secs. 22-188—22-200. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - CARE OF PREMISES STANDARDS 

Sec. 22-201. - Definitions. 
As used in this article: 
Person means any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company, or organization of any kind. 
Property means any real property located within the territorial limits of Upson County, Georgia, but not within the municipal limits of either Thomaston or Yatesville, which does not comprise a street or highway. 
(Ord. No. 175, § 1, 6-28-2005) 
Sec. 22-202. - Violations. 
It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of a building, structure or property in unincorporated Upson County to utilize the premises of such property for the open storage of any and all abandoned items and materials, including, but not limited to, ice boxes, refrigerators, stoves, other types of appliances, glass, building materials, building rubbish, weeds, tree limbs, dead trees, trash, garbage, debris and similar items. 
It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of a building, structure, or property in unincorporated Upson County to keep the premises of such property overgrown with grass, weeds, vines, or other vegetation. This provision shall not apply to owners of properties that are completely vacant and devoid of active land uses other than agricultural uses. 
(Ord. No. 175, § 2, 6-28-2005) 
Sec. 22-203. - Penalties. 
Any person who violates one or more of the provisions of section 22-202 of this article shall be punished in accordance with section 1-11 of the Code of Upson County, Georgia. Generally, this provides for the punishment by a sentence not to exceed 60 days imprisonment or a $1,000.00 fine, or both. 
(Ord. No. 175, § 3, 6-28-2005) 
Sec. 22-204. - Administration. 
It shall be the duty of the code enforcement officer of Upson County to inspect, or cause to be inspected, property located in the county to determine whether or not there are any violations of section 22-202 of this article. Additionally, the zoning administrator and any building official of the county shall have the authority to inspect, or cause to be inspected, property for the presence of such violations. Upon discovery of any such violations, any of these named county officials shall promptly issue a citation to the offending person. 
(Ord. No. 175, § 4, 6-28-2005) 
Chapter 23 - NUISANCE ABATEMENT ORDINANCE 

Sec. 23-1. - Short title. 
This chapter is known as and may be cited as "The Upson County Nuisance Abatement Ordinance." 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 1, 11-10-2009) 
Sec. 23-2. - Intent and purpose. 
The board of commissioners hereby declares it to be the purpose and intent of this chapter to establish a uniform and exclusive summary procedure for use in the abatement of public nuisances in unincorporated Upson County. The provisions hereof are adopted pursuant to the authority provided by The O.C.G.A. § 41-2-7 et seq., as amended by the 2001 Session of the General Assembly. It is the further purpose and intent of this chapter that the procedures established hereunder shall comply with the minimum provisions of O.C.G.A. 41-2-7 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 2, 11-10-2009) 
Sec. 23-3. - Conflicting law. 
The provisions of the 1985 edition of the Standard Unsafe Building Abatement Code, previously adopted by the board of commissioners shall no longer be used for nuisance abatement. Since there are pending cases brought under the Standard Unsafe Building Abatement Code, the provisions thereof may but shall not be required to be used for cases in which a Notice of Unsafe Building was issued prior to the adoption of this the Upson County Nuisance Abatement Ordinance. In all other cases in which a nuisance is complained of, the provisions of this chapter shall govern. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 3, 11-10-2009) 
Sec. 23-4. - Findings. 
The board of commissioners finds that there exist in unincorporated Upson County properties which are unfit for human habitation or for commercial, industrial, or business uses due to dilapidation and which are not in compliance with applicable codes; which have defects increasing the hazards of fire accidents, or other calamities; which lack adequate ventilation, light, or sanitary facilities; which have other conditions that render such properties unsafe or unsanitary, or dangerous or detrimental to the health, safety, or welfare, or otherwise inimical to the welfare of the residents of Upson County; or which are vacant and being used in the commission of drug crimes. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 4, 11-10-2009) 
Sec. 23-5. - Definitions. 
As used throughout this chapter, the term: 
Applicable codes means (1) any optional housing or abatement standard provided in O.C.G.A. tit. 8, ch. 2, including standard minimum codes as adopted now or hereafter by ordinance, or by operation of law, or other property maintenance standards as adopted now or hereafter by ordinance or operation of law, or general nuisance law, relative to the safe use of real property; and (2) any fire or life safety code as provided for in O.C.G.A, tit. 25, ch. 2. Any such building or minimum standard codes for real property improvements shall be deemed to mean those building or minimum standard codes in existence at the time such real property improvements were constructed unless otherwise provided by law. 
Closing means causing a property to be vacated and secured against unauthorized entry. 
Drug crime means an act which is a violation of O.C.G.A. tit. 16, ch. 13, art. 2, known as the "Georgia Controlled Substances Act." 
Owner means both the current owner of record and any current mortgagee holding legal title by virtue of a security instrument as shown by a 50-year title examination conducted in accordance with the title standards of the State Bar of Georgia. 
Parties in interest (for the purposes of service under section 23-8) are the owner and any other persons or entities included within the following categories: 
(1)	Persons in possession of said property and premises; 
(2)	Persons having of record in Upson County any vested right, title, or interest in or lien upon such property based upon a 50-year title examination conducted in accordance with the title standards of the State Bar of Georgia; 
(3)	Persons having paid an occupation tax within the previous calendar year to Upson County for a location or office at the subject building or structure; or 
(4)	Persons having filed a property tax return with the tax commissioner as to the subject property for the most recent tax year in which such returns have become due. 
Property means any lot, tract, or parcel of real estate whether improved or unimproved. It shall include any dwelling, building, structure, or part thereof used and occupied for human habitation or commercial, industrial, or business uses, or intended to be so used, and includes any outhouse, improvement, and appurtenance belonging thereto or usually enjoyed therewith and also includes any building or structure of any design. The term shall expressly include, for means of amplification and not limitation, a swimming pool. Also as used in this chapter, the terms shall not mean or include any farm, any building or structure located on a farm, or any agricultural facility or other building or structure used for the production, growing, raising, harvesting, storage, or processing of crops, livestock, poultry, or other farm products. 
Public authority means any member of the board of commissioners, any housing authority officer, or any officer who is in charge of any department or branch of Upson County Government relating to health, fire, or building regulations or to other activities concerning properties in the county; however, in no event shall any such public authority who files a request for investigation hereunder be the public officer exercising the powers conferred upon public officers under this chapter. 
Public officer means either the head of the county building and zoning office or his or her designee, or the environmental officer of the Upson County Board of Health or his or her designee. 
Repair means altering or improving a property so as to bring any dwelling, building, or structure into compliance with the applicable codes in the jurisdiction where the property is located and/or the cleaning or removal of debris, trash, and other materials present and accumulated which create unsanitary and unsafe conditions which are an endangerment to the public health or safety in or about any property. 
Resident means any person residing in unincorporated Upson County on or after the date on which the alleged nuisance arose. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 5, 11-10-2009) 
Sec. 23-6. - Duties of property owners. 
(a)	It is the duty of the owner of every property located within the unincorporated Upson County: 
(1)	To construct and maintain such property in conformance with applicable codes in force within unincorporated Upson County, or such ordinances which regulate and prohibit activities on property and which declare it to be a public nuisance to construct or maintain any property in violation of such codes or ordinances; and 
(2)	To keep such property clean and free of any materials or conditions which create a health or safety hazard either on such property or to surrounding persons or properties. 
(b)	No owner shall allow any property located within unincorporated Upson County to be used in the commission of drug crimes. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 6, 11-10-2009) 
Sec. 23-7. - Nuisance abatement procedure. 
(a)	Appointment and designation of public officer. Each of the following is hereby appointed and designated as a public officer with the authority to carry out the powers and duties of this Chapter: The Upson County Building Official and the environmental officer of the Upson County Board of Health. Such appointment and designation shall include the designees of such persons. 
(b)	Complaint and investigation. Whenever a request is filed with a public officer by a public authority or by at least five residents of the unincorporated area of the county charging that any property: 
(1)	Is unfit for human habitation or for commercial, industrial, or business use and not in compliance with applicable codes; 
(2)	Is vacant and being used in connection with the commission of drug crimes; or 
(3)	Constitutes an endangerment to the public health or safety as a result of unsanitary or unsafe conditions. 
The public officer with whom the request is filed shall make an investigation or inspection of the specific property. If an inspection is necessary, the public officer shall endeavor to obtain the permission of the owner to conduct such inspection. If permission is withheld, the public officer may seek the assistance of the county attorney's office to obtain an inspection warrant from a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(c)	Judicial complaint and summons. If the public officer's investigation or inspection confirms that any property meets one or more of the three enumerated standards from subsection (b), the public officer may file in a court of competent jurisdiction a complaint in rem against the lot, tract, or parcel of real property wherein the nuisance complained of exists and shall cause summons and a copy of the complaint to be served on the parties in interest of such dwelling, building, or structure pursuant to the provisions of section 23-8. The complaint shall identify the subject real property by appropriate street address and official tax map reference; identify the parties in interest; state with particularity the factual basis for the action; and contain a statement of the action sought by the public officer to abate the alleged nuisance. 
(d)	Time of hearing. The summons shall notify the parties in interest that a hearing will be held before a court of competent jurisdiction at a date and time certain. Such hearing shall be held no sooner than 15 days and no later than 45 days after the filing of said complaint in the proper court. However, in the event that service upon the probate judge is necessary under the provisions of section 23-8, the hearing will be held no sooner than 30 days following service upon the probate judge though still in no event shall the hearing be held more than 45 days after the filing of said complaint. 
(e)	Right to be heard. The parties in interest shall have the right to file an answer to the complaint and to appear in person or by attorney and offer testimony at the time and place fixed for hearing. 
(f)	Order. If, after such notice and hearing, the court determines that the property in question meets one or more of the standards enumerated in subsection (b) so as to constitute a public nuisance, the court shall state in writing findings of fact in support of such determination and shall issue and cause to be served upon the owner and any parties in interest that have answered the complaint or appeared at the hearing an order which does one of the following: 
(1)	If the repair of the said property can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to its present value, the order shall require the owner, within a specified time, to repair such property so as to bring it into full compliance with the applicable codes relevant to the cited violation and, if applicable, to effect a closing of any structure so that it cannot be used in connection with the commission of drug crimes; or 
(2)	If the repair of the said property in order to bring it into full compliance with applicable codes relevant to the cited violations cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the present value thereof, the order shall require the owner, within a specified time, to demolish and remove the noncompliant dwelling, building, or structure and all debris from the property. 
For purposes of this section, in cases in which the nuisance complained of is a dwelling, building, or structure of any kind, the court shall make its determination of 'reasonable cost in relation to the present value' without consideration of the value of the land on which the structure is situated; provided, however, the costs of the preparation necessary to repair a structure may be considered. Income and financial status of the owner shall not be a factor in the court's determination. The present value of the structure and the costs of repair, alteration, or improvement may be established by affidavits of real estate appraisers with a Georgia appraiser classification as provided in O.C.G.A. tit. 43, ch. 39A, qualified building contractors with a current business license to do work in Upson County, or qualified building inspectors without actual testimony presented. Costs of repair, alteration, or improvement of the structure shall be the cost necessary to bring the structure into compliance with the applicable codes relevant to the cited violations 
(g)	Remedies of public officer in the event of noncompliance with order. 
(1)	The order entered under subsection (f) shall further provide that, if the owner fails to comply with an order to repair, demolish, or close the property within the specified time, the public officer may cause such property to be repaired, demolished, or closed, whichever the order required upon approval of the board of commissioners. The public officer is also authorized to file a motion for attachment for contempt against the owner with the court which issued the order as an alternate or additional remedy. 
(2)	If the public officer chooses to have the work done as ordered, he or she shall cause to be posted on the main entrance of the building, dwelling, or structure a placard with the following words: 
This building is unfit for human habitation or commercial, industrial, or business use and does not comply with the applicable codes or has been ordered secured to prevent its use in connection with drug crimes or constitutes an endangerment to public health or safety as a result of unsanitary or unsafe conditions. The use or occupation of this building is prohibited and unlawful. Removal of this notice shall constitute a crime. 
(3)	It shall be unlawful for any person to remove any such posted notice, and anyone who does shall upon conviction be punished as provided by ordinance. The code enforcement officer shall have the authority to cite persons for such unlawful removal. 
(h)	Salvage. If the public officer has a structure demolished, reasonable effort shall be made to salvage reusable materials for credit against the cost of demolition. The proceeds of any moneys received from the sale of salvaged materials shall be used or applied against the cost of the demolition and removal of the structure, and proper records shall be kept showing application of sales proceeds. Any such sale of salvaged materials may be made without the necessity of public advertisement and bid. Neither the public officer nor Upson County shall have any liability resulting from or occasioned by the sale of any such salvaged materials, including, without limitation, defects in such salvaged materials. 
(i)	Lien for costs. The order shall provide that the amount of all costs associated with the abatement action shall be a lien against the real property upon which such costs was incurred. Such costs shall include but not be limited to the cost of demolition, reasonable attorneys' fees and all court costs, appraisal fees, administrative costs incurred by the tax commissioner, restoration to grade of the real property should it be demolished, and title examination costs. The order should recite the amount of costs incurred by the county as of the date of the order. Upon preparing a final statement of costs, the public officer shall prepare a "lien for costs of abatement" detailing any and all such costs. Such lien shall attach to the real property upon the filing of a certified copy of the order requiring repair, closure, or demolition, in the office of the clerk of superior court, and shall relate back to the date of the filing of the lis pendens notice required under section 23-8. The clerk of superior court shall record and index such certified copy of the order in the deed records of the county and enter the lien for costs of abatement on the general execution docket. Such lien should cross-reference the order and include the original caption and case number from the nuisance abatement action. The lien shall be superior to all other liens on the property, except liens for taxes to which the lien shall be inferior, and shall continue in force until paid in full. After filing a certified copy of the order with the clerk of superior court, the public officer shall forward a copy of the order and a final statement of costs to the tax commissioner. 
(j)	Enforcement of lien. It shall be the duty of the tax commissioner to collect the amount of the lien in conjunction with the collection of ad valorem taxes on the property; however, the tax commissioner shall be authorized to bill the amount of the lien as it comes due separately from the annual ad valorem tax bill in order to ensure prompt notice of the amount of the lien and so as to not interfere with the regular billing cycle of the annual ad valorem taxes. The tax commissioner shall have the full authority to collect the amount of the lien as if it were a real property ad valorem tax, using all methods available for collecting real property ad valorem taxes, including specifically O.C.G.A. tit. 48, ch. 4; provided, however, that the limitation of O.C.G.A. § 48-4-78 which requires 12 months of delinquency before commencing a tax foreclosure shall not apply. The tax commissioner shall remit the amount collected to the general fund of the county. Thirty days after imposition of the lien, the unpaid lien amount shall bear interest and penalties in the same amount as applicable to interest and penalties on unpaid real property ad valorem taxes. 
(k)	Waiver of lien. The board of commissioners may waive and release any such lien imposed on property of the owner for costs incurred by the county up to the time of the entry of the order and any additional costs incurred subsequent thereto in attempting to bring the property into compliance by entering into a contract with the owner in which the owner agrees to a timetable for rehabilitation of the real property or the dwelling, building, or structure on the property and demonstrates the financial means to accomplish such rehabilitation. 
(l)	Appellate procedure. Where the abatement action does not commence in the superior court, review of a court order requiring the repair, alteration, improvement, or demolition of a property shall be by direct appeal to the superior court under O.C.G.A. § 5-3-29. 
(m)	Alternate remedies. Nothing in this section shall be construed as to limit or impair the authority of public officers or other county employees under existing and future ordinances to issue citations for violations of state minimum standard codes, optional building, fire, life safety, and other codes adopted by ordinance, and conditions creating a public health hazard or general nuisance, and to seek to enforce such citations in a court of competent jurisdiction prior to issuing a complaint in rem as provided in this chapter. The issuance of a citation for a violation of any such codes shall not be required as a prerequisite to issuing a complaint in rem under this section. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 7, 11-10-2009) 
Sec. 23-8. - Service and notice. 
(a)	Copies of the complaint and summons shall be served in each of the following ways as applicable: 
(1)	In all cases, by conspicuously posting a copy on the subject dwelling, building, structure, or property within three days of the filing of the complaint. 
(2)	In all cases, by mailing a copy to the property address by first class mail addressed to the attention of the occupants, if any. 
(3)	By personal service upon each party in interest if the identity and whereabouts of said parties are reasonably ascertainable and if such parties are residents of the county. Service shall be perfected at least ten days prior to the date of the hearing. Service may be made by the public officer designated by ordinance to abate nuisances, by any law enforcement officer of the county, by the code enforcement officer or by permanent process server; and a return of service, filed with the clerk of the appropriate court, shall be deemed sufficient proof that service was perfected. 
(4)	By certified mail or statutory overnight delivery, return receipt requested to the most recent address shown in county tax records and real estate records and mailed at least 14 days prior to the date of the hearing if any party in interest is a resident of this state but resides outside of the county or if any party in interest is a nonresident of this state, if the addresses are known. 
(5)	By publication for nonresidents and residents of the state who reside outside of the county whose mailing addresses are unknown. A notice stating the date, time, and place of the hearing shall be published in the newspaper in which the sheriffs advertisements appear in such county once a week for two consecutive weeks prior to the hearing. 
(6)	By personal service upon a guardian or other personal representative in the event that any party in interest is a minor, an estate, an incompetent person, or person laboring under disabilities. If such guardian or personal representative resides outside the county or is a nonresident of this state, he or she shall be served as provided for in paragraphs (4) and (5) of this section. If such party in interest has no guardian or personal representative, service shall be perfected by personally serving the judge of the probate court at least 30 days prior to the date of the hearing which judge shall stand in the place of and protect the rights of such minor, estate, or incompetent person or appoint a guardian ad litem for such person. 
(7)	By personal service upon the judge of the probate court in the event of unknown persons or unborn remaindermen who are likely to have any rights in the property or interest in the proceeds thereof. Service shall be perfected at least 30 days prior to the date of the hearing, and it shall be the duty of the judge of the probate court to stand in the place of and protect the rights of such unknown parties or unborn remaindermen. 
(8)	By publication in all other cases where the whereabouts of any party in interest is unknown and the same cannot be ascertained by the public officer in the exercise of reasonable diligence or if any party in interest cannot, after due diligence, be served as provided in this section. In such event, the public officer shall make an affidavit to that effect and serve by publication in the manner provided in paragraph (5) of this Code section, and such publication shall be sufficient proof that service was perfected. 
(b)	A notice of lis pendens shall be filed in the office of the clerk of superior court in the county in which the dwelling, building, or structure is located at the time of filing the complaint in the appropriate court. Such notice shall have the same force and effect as other lis pendens notices provided by law. 
(c)	Orders and other filings made subsequent to service of the initial complaint and summons shall be served in the manner provided in this section or in O.C.G.A. tit. 41, ch. 2, § 12, including certified mail or statutory overnight delivery, return receipt requested, on any party in interest who answers the complaint or appears at the hearing. Any party who fails to answer or appear at the hearing shall be deemed to have waived all further notice in the proceedings. 
(Ord. No. 187, § 3, 12-12-2006; Ord. No. 211, § 8, 11-10-2009)

ARTICLE II. - OCCUPATION TAXES AND REGULATORY FEES[2] 

Footnotes:
