Expansion to an existing manufactured home park or subdivision means the preparation of additional sites by the construction of facilities for servicing the lots on which the manufactured homes are to be affixed, including the installation of utilities, the construction of streets, and either final site grading or the pouring of concrete pads. 
Flood or flooding means a general and temporary condition of partial or complete inundation of normally dry land areas from: 
(1)	The overflow of inland or tidal waters; or 
(2)	The unusual and rapid accumulation or runoff of surface waters from any source. 
Flood hazard boundary map (FHBM) means an official map of a community, issued by the Federal Insurance Administration, where the boundaries of areas of special flood hazard have been defined as zone A. 
Flood insurance rate map (FIRM) means an official map of a community, issued by the Federal Insurance Administration, delineating the areas of special flood hazard and/or risk premium zones applicable to the county. 
Flood insurance study the official report by the Federal Insurance Administration evaluating flood hazards and containing flood profiles and water surface elevations of the base flood. 
Floodplain means any land area susceptible to flooding. 
Flood proofing means any combination of structural and non-structural additions, changes, or adjustments to structures, which reduce or eliminate flood damage to real estate or improved real property, water and sanitary facilities, structures and their contents. 
Floodway means the channel of a river or other watercourse and the adjacent land areas that must be reserved in order to discharge the base flood without cumulatively increasing the water surface elevation more than a designated height. 
Freeboard means a factor of safety usually expressed in feet above a flood level for purposes of floodplain management. Freeboard tends to compensate for the many unknown factors that could contribute to flood heights greater than the height calculated for a selected datum, to which base flood elevations shown on a community's flood insurance rate map are referenced. 
National Geodetic Vertical Datum (NGVD) as corrected in 1929 is a vertical control used as a reference for establishing varying elevations within the floodplain. 
New construction means, for the purposes of determining insurance rates, structures for which the "start of construction" commenced after May 17, 1989, and includes any subsequent improvements to such structures. For floodplain management purposes, "new construction" means structures for which the "start of construction" commenced after May 17, 1989, and includes any subsequent improvements to such structures. 
New manufactured home park or subdivision means a manufactured home park or subdivision for which the construction of facilities for servicing the lots on which the manufactured homes are to be affixed (including at a minimum, the installation of utilities, the construction of streets, and either final site grading or the pouring of concrete pads) is completed after May 17, 1989. 
North American Vertical Datum (NAVD) has replaced the National Geodetic Vertical Datum of 1929 in existing and future FEMA flood modernization maps. 
Recreational vehicle means a vehicle, which is: 
(1)	Built on a single chassis; 
(2)	Four hundred square feet or less when measured at the largest horizontal projection; 
(3)	Designed to be self-propelled or permanently towable by a light duty truck; and 
(4)	Designed primarily not for use as a permanent dwelling but as temporary living quarters for recreational, camping, travel, or seasonal use. 
Start of construction means the date the development permit was issued, provided the actual start of construction, repair, reconstruction, or improvement was within 180 days of the permit date. The actual start means the first placement of permanent construction of the structure such as the pouring of slabs or footings, installation of piles, construction of columns, or any work beyond the stage of excavation, and includes the placement of a manufactured home on a foundation. Permanent construction does not include initial land preparation, such as clearing, grading and filling; nor does it include the installation of streets and/or walkways; nor does it include excavation for a basement, footings, piers or foundations or the erection of temporary forms; nor does it include the installation on the property of buildings appurtenant to the permitted structure, such as garages or sheds not occupied as dwelling units or part of the main structure. (Note: Accessory structures are not exempt from any ordinance requirements.) For a substantial improvement, the actual start of construction means the first alteration of any wall, ceiling, floor, or other structural part of a building, whether or not that alteration affects the external dimensions of the building. 
Structure means a walled and roofed building that is principally above ground, a manufactured home, a gas or liquid storage tank. 
Subdivision means the division of a single lot into three or more lots for the purpose of sale or development. 
Substantial damage means damage of any origin sustained by a structure whereby the cost of restoring the structure to its before damaged condition would equal or exceed 50 percent of the market value of the structure before the damage occurred. 
Substantial improvement means any reconstruction, rehabilitation, addition, or other improvement of a structure, taking place during a five-year period, in which the cumulative cost equals or exceeds 50 percent of the market value of the structure prior to the "start of construction" of the improvement. Note: The market value of the structure should be (1) the appraised value of the structure prior to the start of the initial repair or improvement, or (2) in the case of damage, the value of the structure prior to the damage occurring. This term includes structures, which have incurred "substantial damage", regardless of the actual amount of repair work performed. 
For the purposes of this definition, "substantial improvement" is considered to occur when the first alteration of any wall, ceiling, floor, or other structural part of the building commences, whether or not that alteration affects the external dimensions of the building. The term does not, however, include (1) those improvements of a structure required to comply with existing violations of state or local health, sanitary, or safety code specifications which are solely necessary to assure safe living conditions and which have been identified by the code enforcement official, and not solely triggered by an improvement or repair project, or (2) any alteration of a "historic structure" provided that the alteration will not preclude the structure's continued designation as a "historic structure". 
Substantially improved existing manufactured home parks or subdivisions is where the repair, reconstruction, rehabilitation or improvement of the streets, utilities and pads equals or exceeds 50 percent of the value of the streets, utilities and pads before the repair, reconstruction or improvement commenced. 
Variance means a grant of relief from the requirements of this article, which permits construction in a manner otherwise prohibited by this article. 
Violation means the failure of a structure or other development to be fully compliant with the county's floodplain management regulations. A structure or other development without the elevation certificate, or other certifications, or other evidence of compliance required by this article is presumed to be in violation until such time as that documentation is provided. 
(Ord. No. 210, art. 6, 9-22-2009) 
Secs. 42-82—42-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 7. - SEVERABILITY 

Sec. 42-91. - Severability. 
Should any sentence, paragraph or section of this article be declared to be invalid for any reason, such declaration shall not affect the validity of any other sentence, paragraph or section of this article and all such remaining sentences, paragraphs and sections hereof shall remain valid and of full force and effect, and the board of commissioners of Upson County, Georgia, hereby declare that such continuing validity of the remaining portions hereof is its intent as of the date of the enactment hereof. 
(Ord. No. 210, art. 7, 9-22-2009)

Chapter 50 - HISTORICAL PRESERVATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Buildings and building regulations, ch. 22; environment, ch. 38; planning, ch. 66; utilities, ch. 90; historic districts, app. A, § 2201 et seq.; zoning, app. A. 
State Law reference— Georgia Register of Historic Places, O.C.G.A. § 12-3-50.2; fire safety requirements for historic buildings or structures, O.C.G.A. § 25-2-13; grants to municipal corporations for repairs on facilities of historical value, O.C.G.A. § 36-40-1; Georgia Uniform Conservation Easement Act, O.C.G.A. § 44-10-1 et seq.; Georgia Historic Preservation Act, O.C.G.A. § 44-10-20 et seq.; historic preservation commissions, O.C.G.A. § 44-10-24; historic landmark or district designation procedure, O.C.G.A. § 44-10-26; certificates of appropriateness, O.C.G.A. § 44-10-28; certification as rehabilitated historic property for purposes of preferential assessment, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-7.2; landmark historic property for purposes of ad valorem taxation, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-7.3; the Uniform Act for the Application of Building and Fire Related Codes to Existing Buildings, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-200 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 50-1—50-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - HISTORIC PRESERVATION COMMISSION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2. 

Sec. 50-26. - Findings; established. 
(a)	For the purposes of this article, the board of commissioners finds as follows: 
(1)	The county is in possession of properties of historical, cultural and esthetic value; 
(2)	The board of commissioners is desirous of protecting, enhancing, and preserving such properties; 
(3)	The state general assembly has found that the historical, cultural, and esthetic heritage of this state is among its most valued and important assets and that the preservation of this heritage is essential to the promotion of the health, prosperity, and general welfare of the people, and has pursuant to O.C.G.A. §§ 44-10-20—44-10-28 provided for the establishing of a historic preservation commission; and 
(4)	O.C.G.A. § 44-10-24 provides that the local governing body of the county shall determine the number of members of the commission, which shall be at least three, and the length of their terms, which shall be no greater than four years, and a majority of the members of any such commission shall have demonstrated special interest, experience, or education in history or architecture and all shall serve without compensation. 
(b)	Therefore, a commission known as the Upson County Historic Preservation Commission is established, subject to this article. 
(Ord. No. 47, 1-27-1989) 
Sec. 50-27. - Members. 
The historic preservation commission shall consist of four members who are residents of the county and have demonstrated special interest in the preservation of the county's historic properties. 
(Ord. No. 47, § 1, 1-27-1989) 
Sec. 50-28. - Term of office. 
Members of the historic preservation commission shall be appointed by the board of commissioners to serve staggered terms of four years. 
(Ord. No. 47, § 2, 1-27-1989) 
Sec. 50-29. - Powers and duties. 
Members of the historic preservation commission shall be authorized to: 
(1)	Prepare an inventory of all property within its respective historic preservation jurisdiction having the potential for designation as historic property. 
(2)	Recommend to the board of commissioners specific places, districts, sites, buildings, structures or works of art to be designated by ordinance as historic properties or historic districts. 
(3)	Review applications for certificates of appropriateness and grant or deny the certificates in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 44-10-28. 
(4)	Recommend to the board of commissioners that the designation of any place, district, site, building, structure, or work of art as a historic property or as a historic district be revoked or removed. 
(5)	Restore or preserve any historic properties acquired by the county. 
(6)	Promote the acquisition by the board of commissioners of facade easements and conservation easements in accordance with O.C.G.A. §§ 44-10-1—44-10-5. 
(7)	Conduct an educational program on historic properties located within its historic preservation jurisdiction. 
(8)	Make such investigations and studies of matters relating to historic preservation as the board of commissioners or the historic preservation commission itself may from time to time deem necessary or appropriate for the purposes of this article. 
(9)	Seek out state and federal funds for historic preservation and make recommendations to the board of commissioners concerning the most appropriate use of any funds acquired. 
(10)	Consult with historic preservation experts in the historic preservation section of the department of natural resources or its successor and the Georgia Trust for Historic Preservation, Inc. 
(11)	Submit to the historic preservation section of the department of natural resources or its successor a list of historic properties or historic districts designated as such pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 44-10-26. 
(12)	Adopt such rules, regulations and procedures as may be deemed necessary or desirable for the conduct of the business of the historic preservation commission. 
(13)	Hold as trustee for the county such leases, agreements, titles, interest and easements to historic properties that are owned or acquired by the county. 
(14)	Establish such reasonable rules, regulations and procedures as may be necessary for the enjoyment of historic properties by the general public. 
(Ord. No. 47, § 3, 1-27-1989) 
Chapter 54 - MANUFACTURED HOMES AND TRAILERS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Buildings and building regulations, ch. 22; environment, ch. 38; floods, ch. 42; health and sanitation, ch. 46; planning, ch. 66; roads and bridges, ch. 70; solid waste, ch. 74; subdivisions, ch. 78; utilities, ch. 90; zoning, app. A. 
State Law reference— Registration and licensing of dealers, manufacturers and persons transporting mobile homes, O.C.G.A. § 40-2-38; removal of transportable housing from lands subject to writ of possession, O.C.G.A. § 44-7-59; ad valorem taxation of mobile homes, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-440 et seq.; issuance of mobile home location permits, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-492; display of decals, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-492; the Uniform Standards Code for Manufactured Homes Act, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-130 et seq.; classification of mobile homes as a separate class of property for ad valorem property tax purposes, Ga. Const. art. VII, § I, ¶ III. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 54-1. - Provisions saved from repeal. 
Ordinance No. 45, adopted January 22, 1993, on the subject of manufactured housing regulations, is not repealed and shall continue in full force and effect pending a revision of the subject matter by the county. 
Secs. 54-2—54-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MANUFACTURED HOME DECALS AND REPORTS BY MANUFACTURED HOME PARK OPERATORS 

Sec. 54-21. - Decal required. 
(a)	All persons owning a manufactured home based in Upson County on January 1 of each year shall obtain from the tax commissioner a decal before May 1, as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-5-492. This requirement pertains to all manufactured homes, including those exempt from taxation by homestead exemption or other provisions of state law. 
(b)	Such decals shall be affixed to the mobile homes in such a manner as to cause them to be easily visible for inspection. 
(c)	Owners of manufactured homes locating in the county after January 1 of any year shall be required to report their mobile homes to the office of the tax commissioner within ten working days. 
(Ord. No. 176, § 1, 8-23-2005) 
Sec. 54-22. - Reports by manufactured home park operators. 
(a)	Every owner and operator of a manufactured home park is required to give the tax assessors an inventory of all manufactured homes based in the park as of October 1 of each year. This shall be done no later than October 15 of each year. The tax assessors shall make available an inventory of records as of October 1. 
(b)	Every owner, manager, and operator of a manufactured home park is required to report to the tax assessors any manufactured home removal from the park prior to said home being removed, if known to the park manager, operator or owner. 
(c)	Every owner, manager and operator of a manufactured home park shall furnish to the tax assessors an updated lot map of each park, and any changes shall be reported by January 1 of each year. 
(d)	Every owner, manager and operator of a manufactured home park is required to notify the tax assessors of any change in ownership or of name of any manufactured home park within 30 days of such change. 
(Ord. No. 176, § 2, 8-23-2005) 
Sec. 54-23. - Penalties. 
Any person who violates one or more of the provisions of this article shall be punished in accordance with section 1-11 of the Code of Upson County, Georgia. Generally, this provides for the punishment by a sentence not to exceed 60 days imprisonment or a $1,000.00 fine, or both. 
(Ord. No. 176, § 3, 8-23-2005) 
Sec. 54-24. - Administration. 
It shall be the duty of the code enforcement officer of Upson County to inspect, or cause to be inspected, property located in the county to determine whether or not there are any violations of this article. Upon discovery of any such violations, the code enforcement officer may issue a citation to the offending person. 
(Ord. No. 176, § 1, 8-23-2005) 
Chapter 58 - OFFENSES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Courts, ch. 34; traffic and vehicles, ch. 86. 
State Law reference— Criminal Code of Georgia, O.C.G.A. § 16-1-1 et seq.; limitation on home rule powers of municipal corporations with respect to duplication of state criminal offenses, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(2). 

Sec. 58-1. - Public drunkenness. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to be and appear in an intoxicated condition in any public place or upon any private property not his own, which condition is made manifest by: 
(1)	Boisterousness; 
(2)	Indecent condition or act; or 
(3)	Vulgar, profane, loud, or unbecoming language. 
(b)	The accused may be arrested by law enforcement officers upon being charged with a violation of this section. 
(c)	Violation of this section shall, upon conviction, be punishable as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 76, §§ 1, 3, 4, 4-15-1994) 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6. 
State Law reference— Public drunkenness, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41. 
Sec. 58-2. - Disorderly conduct. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to do any of the following: 
(1)	Engage in a fight; 
(2)	Act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another person whereby such person is placed in reasonable fear of the safety of such person's life, limb, or health; 
(3)	Act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another person whereby the property of such person is placed in danger of being damaged or destroyed; 
(4)	Without provocation, uses to or of another person in such other person's presence opprobrious, vulgar, profane, or abusive words which by their very utterance tend to incite to an immediate breach of the peace; words commonly known as fighting words which, as a matter of common knowledge and under ordinary circumstances, will, when used to or of another person in such other person's presence, naturally tend to provoke violent resentment; or 
(5)	Without provocation, use obscene, vulgar, or profane language in the presence of or by telephone to a person under the age of 14 years which threatens an immediate breach of the peace. 
(b)	A person accused of committing any of the acts prohibited by this section may be arrested by law enforcement officers upon being charged with such violation. 
(c)	Violation of this section shall, upon conviction, be punishable as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 76, § 4, 4-15-1994; Ord. No. 104, §§ 2—4, 6-26-1997) 
Sec. 58-3. - Public indecency. 
(a)	For the purposes of this section, the term "public place" shall mean any place where the conduct involved may reasonably be expected to be viewed by people other than members of the actor's family or household. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person to commit an act of public indecency. A person commits the offense of public indecency when the person performs any of the following acts in a public place: 
(1)	An act of sexual intercourse; 
(2)	A lewd exposure of the male or female genitals, pubic area, buttocks, or female breasts; 
(3)	A lewd appearance in a state of partial or complete nudity; or 
(4)	A lewd caress or indecent fondling of oneself or the body of another person. 
(c)	Violation of this section shall, upon conviction, be punishable as provided in section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 105, §§ 1—3, 6-26-1997) 
Sec. 58-4. - Abandoned personal property. 
(a)	When personal property has been placed upon or adjacent to a public right-of-way upon the execution of a writ of possession pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 44-7-50 et seq., such personal property is presumed to be abandoned on the third calendar day following the execution of the writ of possession. 
(b)	Any such abandoned personal property remaining on or adjacent to a public right-of-way shall be removed and disposed of by the real property owner and the person executing the affidavit for writ of possession not later than the fifth calendar day following the execution of the writ of possession. 
(c)	Failure of the real property owner and the person executing the affidavit for writ of possession to remove any abandoned personal property placed on or adjacent to a public right-of-way, pursuant to writ of possession, as required under this section, shall be a violation and punishable as provided by section 1-11. 
(Ord. No. 151, §§ 1—3, 11-8-2001) 
Chapter 62 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— By agreement dated April 16, 1998, Upson County and the City of Thomaston reestablished the Thomaston-Upson County Recreation Commission. The agreement provides for appointment of members, their terms, oath, meetings, duties and other matters. An official copy of the agreement is on file in the office of the county clerk. 
Cross reference— Environment, ch. 38. 
State Law reference— State parks, O.C.G.A. § 12-3-1 et seq.; establishment of recreation systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-64-1 et seq.; recreation boards, O.C.G.A. § 36-64-5; Georgia State Games Commission, O.C.G.A. § 50-12-40 et seq.; power to provide parks, recreation areas, programs and facilities, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(5). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 62-1. - County parks and recreation areas. 
(a)	Upson County has established and maintains public parks and recreation areas outside the limits of municipal corporations. 
(b)	The public parks and recreation areas established by Upson County are available to the public during daylight hours, except that any program or activity sponsored by the Thomaston-Upson County Recreation Department shall have priority in the use of park facilities for its scheduled activities, and is authorized to expend its use of said facilities beyond daylight hours. The hours of operation of Sprewell Bluff Park are subject to change on a permanent or temporary basis by the Upson County Board of Commissioners to include beyond daylight hours. 
(Ord. No. 223, § 1.A, 5-14-2013; Ord. No. 224, § 1.A, 6-11-2013; Ord. No. 230, § 2.A, 5-27-2014) 
Sec. 62-2. - County property. 
(a)	Upson County owns and maintains property which is not a part of the county public parks and recreation areas. 
(b)	Any person, group or organization desiring to use county property for an event must first apply at the office of the Upson County Commissioners for a permit, no later than 30 days prior to the desired date of use. The application for a permit shall specify among other things, if there will be any food sales or other commercial activity. If so, the applicant must provide evidence of appropriate licenses and permits by those individuals or organizations desiring to sell food or conduct other commercial activities, and must also pay, in advance, a sum to reimburse the actual cost of health or other inspections undertaken by, or on behalf of, Upson County. 
(Ord. No. 223, § 1.B, 5-14-2013; Ord. No. 224, § 1.B, 6-11-2013; Ord. No. 230, § 2.B, 5-27-2014) 
Sec. 62-3. - Rules and regulations. 
(a)	The cardinal rule of conduct for all persons utilizing public parks and recreations areas is that of common courtesy and respect for the rights of others. Most problems can be avoided if this rule is recognized. 
(b)	The possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages within any public park or recreation area is prohibited. Glass containers are prohibited. 
(c)	Motorized vehicles may be operated only upon designated roadways and shall be parked only in officially designated areas. 
(d)	Pets are not permitted within any public park or recreation area unless on a six-foot leash. Owners or handlers are responsible for clean-up/removal of animal feces. Aggressive dogs are not allowed, nor are aggressive breeds. 
(e)	Public parks and recreation areas are to be maintained as peaceful, family recreation areas. Loud radios or other sound systems which can be heard more than 50 feet from the source shall be unlawful. 
(f)	Every person shall at all times obey and comply with directions given by designated employees of Upson County and official regulatory signs posted within any public park or recreation area. 
(Ord. No. 223, § 1.C, 5-14-2013; Ord. No. 224, § 1.C, 6-11-2013; Ord. No. 230, § 2.C, 5-27-2014) 
Secs. 62-4—62-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - SPREWELL BLUFF PARK AND RECREATION AREA 

Sec. 62-21. - Sprewell Bluff Park and Recreation Area. 
(a)	Upson County has leased and maintains the Sprewell Bluff Park and adjacent area at Sprewell Bluff on the Flint River. Sprewell Bluff Park and Recreation Area is defined as being the former Sprewell Bluff State Park or WMA and the 93 plus acres owned by Upson County adjacent to the park. 
(b)	No commercial activity shall be conducted on any part of the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area without FIRST obtaining the approval and consent of the board of commissioners of Upson County and second obtaining a permit from the office of the Upson County Commissioners and payment of the permit fee as established from time to time by the Upson County Board of Commissioners. Non-profit, charitable and civic organizations shall have priority in the approval and issuance of such permits. 
(c)	Vehicle parking fees shall be established by the Upson County Board of Commissioners. 
(d)	In addition to the general rules set out in this chapter, the following Rules and Regulations are applicable to the Upson County Sprewell Bluff Park and Recreation Area: 
(1)	The cardinal rule of conduct for all persons utilizing the Sprewell Bluff Park and Recreation Area is that of common courtesy and respect for the rights of others. Most problems can be avoided if this rule is recognized. 
(2)	No person may be admitted to use the facilities of Sprewell Bluff Park and Recreation Area without payment of the appropriate parking fee. Evidence of fee payment shall be produced upon request of area personnel or other authorized individual. 
(3)	All persons using the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area shall comply with all of the laws of the State of Georgia regulating parks, recreation areas, and fishing, as well as with the applicable rules of the state department of natural resources and of the county. 
(4)	Hunting, trapping or otherwise pursuing or catching any wildlife within the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area is strictly prohibited. 
(5)	Sprewell Bluff opens at 7:00 a.m. and closes at dark throughout the year unless otherwise established by the Upson County Board of Commissioners. 
(6)	Off-road vehicles (ATV's, dirt bikes, off road bicycles, go carts, motorized scooters, etc.) as well as horseback riding are prohibited. Golf carts are likewise prohibited with the exception of those utilized by disabled individuals and displaying a valid handicap sticker, and they are only to be used on paved roadways and at the river side park. 
(7)	The possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages within the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area is prohibited. Glass containers are prohibited. 
(8)	Discharge of any firearm within the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area shall be unlawful. 
(9)	Possession of any explosive substance, including fireworks, within the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area shall be unlawful. 
(10)	Motorized vehicles may be operated only upon designated roadways and shall be parked only in officially designated areas. 
(11)	No person shall drive any motor vehicles of any character on the roadways of the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area at a speed greater than 25 miles per hour or in the river side parking area greater than 15 miles per hour. 
(12)	Pets are not permitted within the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area unless on a six-foot leash. Owners or handlers are responsible for clean-up/removal of animal feces. Aggressive dogs are not allowed, nor are aggressive breeds. 
(13)	Campfires or other open flames shall be unlawful, other than a grill being used in the preparation of food. 
(14)	The park is to be maintained as a peaceful, family recreation area. Loud radios or other sound systems which can be heard more than 50 feet from the source shall be unlawful. 
(15)	The county boat ramp is to be used only in launching or removing boats from the water. Boat ramps must not be blocked. Use of the boat ramp for sunbathing and the placing thereon of lawn chairs and other equipment is prohibited. 
(16)	Every person shall at all times obey and comply with directions given by designated employees of Upson County and official regulatory signs posted within the area. 
(17)	Utilization of the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area and its facilities is at the risk of the user. Swimming is permitted, but there is no life guard on duty at any time. The county assumes no responsibility for injury to persons or property arising from the utilization of the Sprewell Bluff Recreation Area. 
(Ord. No. 223, § 2, 5-14-2013; Ord. No. 224, § 2, 6-11-2013; Ord. No. 230, § 3, 5-27-2014) 
Chapter 66 - PLANNING[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2; buildings and building regulations, ch. 22; environment, ch. 38; floods, ch. 42; historical preservation, ch. 50; manufactured homes and trailers, ch. 54; roads and bridges, ch. 70; subdivisions, ch. 78; utilities, ch. 90; zoning, app. A. 
State Law reference— City Business Improvement District Act, O.C.G.A. § 36-43-1 et seq.; Redevelopment Powers Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-44-1 et seq.; the Zoning Procedures Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1 et seq.; conflicts of interest in zoning actions, O.C.G.A. § 36-67-A-1 et seq.; coordinated and comprehensive planning by counties and municipalities, O.C.G.A. § 36-70-1 et seq.; regional development centers, O.C.G.A. § 50-8-30 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 66-1. - Comprehensive plan adopted. 
The Comprehensive Plan for Upson County, having been approved by the state department of community affairs following a resolution by the board of commissioners to submit such plan on March 8, 1996, is adopted. 
(Res of 6-14-1996) 
State Law reference— Coordinated and comprehensive planning by counties and municipalities, O.C.G.A. § 36-70-1 et seq. 
Secs. 66-2—66-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PLANNING COMMISSION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2. 
State Law reference— Conflicts of interest in zoning actions, O.C.G.A. § 36-67-A-1 et seq.; code of ethics for members of boards, commissions and authorities, O.C.G.A. § 45-10-3. 

Sec. 66-31. - Created. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1(2)(b)(1), the Upson County Planning Commission, referred to in this article as "the planning commission," is created and established. 
(Ord. No. 77, § 103, 6-10-1994) 
Sec. 66-32. - Membership and appointments. 
(a)	The planning commission shall consist of at least three but no more than five members. 
(b)	All members must reside within the unincorporated areas of the county, and they shall be appointed by the board of commissioners. 
(c)	None of the members of the planning commission may hold any other public office; however, they may also be members of the Thomaston-Upson County Planning Commission. 
(d)	Commission members may be removed by the board of commissioners for cause, upon written charges, and after a public hearing. 
(e)	Members of the planning commission will be disqualified to act upon any matter before the planning commission in which they have a personal financial interest or other conflict of interest. 
(Ord. No. 77, § 105, 6-10-1994; Ord. No. 252 , § 1, 11-22-2016) 
Sec. 66-33. - Terms of office. 
(a)	Subject to subsection (b) of this section, the term of each member of the planning commission is for three years. Any vacancy in the membership will be filled for the unexpired term of the vacating member. 
(b)	The three-year terms of all previously appointed members of the planning commission which are being served as of January 27, 2000, shall remain unchanged by Ordinance No. 133, except that the terms of Jimmy Robinson and Joel Pitts are extended an additional seven months such that their terms shall expire on January 9, 2004. 
(c)	The planning commissioner who is to be appointed to complete county commissioner-Elect James Ellington's unexpired term, set to expire December 31, 2017, shall instead be appointed for a full three-year term to end December 31, 2019, therefore creating a three-year cycle of planning commissioner terms, with no more than two commissioners per year completing their terms. 
(Ord. No. 77, § 106, 6-10-1994; Ord. No. 133, § 1, 1-27-2000; Ord. No. 251 , § 1, 11-22-2016) 
Sec. 66-34. - Compensation. 
Planning commission members will receive compensation for their service as determined by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. No. 77, § 107, 6-10-1994) 
Sec. 66-35. - Officers; rules and procedures. 
(a)	The planning commission will elect one of its members as chairman in January of each year. The chairman will serve for one year. At the end of that term, he must either be reelected or a successor elected. 
(b)	The planning commission will appoint a secretary, who may be an officer of the county or the planning commission. 
(c)	The planning commission has the authority to adopt rules of procedure which are consistent with the policies and procedures set out in the county zoning ordinance in appendix A to this Code. 
(d)	Meetings of the planning commission will be held at the call of the chairman or in his absence the acting chairman. 
(e)	The chairman or the acting chairman may administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses by subpoena. The planning commission must keep minutes of its proceedings, showing the vote of each member upon each question or, if absent or failing to vote, indicating such a fact. The planning commission must also keep records of its examinations and other official actions, all of which must be immediately filed in the office of the planning commission and will be public record. 
(f)	A decision of the planning commission must be recorded in the minutes for the meeting at which the decision was made and must contain a statement of the grounds for its decision or action. The full text of the decision must be sent to the applicant. 
(g)	No application requesting the same action for the same property will be received or heard by the planning commission twice within the same 12-month period. However, that limitation does not affect the right of the planning commission to grant a rehearing as provided in the rules and procedures adopted by the planning commission. 
(Ord. No. 77, § 108, 6-10-1994) 
Sec. 66-36. - Purpose and powers. 
(a)	The purpose of the planning commission is as follows: 
(1)	Advise the board of commissioners on applications for amendment to the county zoning ordinance in appendix A to this Code by examining amendment applications and providing written recommendations with reasons for the recommendation to the board of commissioners as specified in section 410 of such ordinance. 
(2)	Dispense general information about the county zoning ordinance to the public upon request. 
(3)	Propose amendments to the county zoning ordinance. 
(4)	Maintain and update the county land use plan (where one exists) so that it may provide a current database with which decisions on proposed amendments to the county zoning ordinance may be made that utilize sound planning principles. 
(5)	Carry out an ongoing comprehensive planning program which, like the land use plan (where one exists), will provide current data on which decisions regarding the county zoning ordinance may be based that utilize sound planning principles. 
(6)	Advise the board of commissioners on matters of zoning and annexation, as appropriate. 
(7)	Authorize variances according to procedures specified in section 407 of the county zoning ordinance. 
(8)	Accept applications for appeal of an action of the administrative officer and render official decisions on them according to procedures specified in section 406 of the county zoning ordinance. 
(9)	Authorize special exceptions under procedures contained in section 409 of the county zoning ordinance. 
(10)	Accept applications for appeal of actions of the historic preservation commission and render official decisions on them. 
(b)	The planning commission does not have the power to: 
(1)	Amend any zoning ordinance; 
(2)	Rezone any land; 
(3)	Declare the county zoning ordinance or any amendment thereto invalid; or 
(4)	Allow any use not permitted by the zoning ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 77, § 104, 6-10-1994)
